<Author>Shoegal81
<Content>Hotel Metro didnt disappoint! My Boyfriend and I were treated to a getaway for our Christmas as an early present and stayed from 16/12 - 22/12We had originally booked hotel Pennsylvania but thanks to reviews on tripadvisor we rebooked as it seemed a nightmare!On arrival we were booked in promptly by Eva, (who is a bit abrupt it has to be said - she wasnt patient when explaining the credit card approval needed for check in, which i thought was a bit rude) i cheekily asked for an upgrade as lots of reviews said this happened often, i was told we already had one with a queen bed, im not sure if this is the case but the room was lovely anyway.the room was warm, fairly spacious, and clean with a huge cupboard which enabled all our shopping to be stowed away in, plus 2 large suitcases, this was a lot of stuff!!The bathroom was fine, clean with loads of toiletries, and the shower was good, water pressure a bit too much for me but my bf loved it. Hairdryer and iron/ironing board were already in the room, as was a safe in the massive cupboard.Fresh towels provided everyday - and the room was cleaned regularly,. On 2 occaisons we had a problem with the room phone, but an engineer was sent up to repair it on both times and then it was fine. Dont use the phone to call international, buy a phonecard where you can call internationally and the minutes you use are deducted from the calling card, not billed to your room, which i was told, is an extortionate rate, if you use the card you are only charged 1 dollar per connected call, regardless of the length.The rooftop terrace has fabulous views of ESB and is worth a look, the coffee room always had fresh tea and coffee on tap, we didnt have breakfast in the hotel, we went to PAX just round the corner, there food is amazing, definately have a tossed salad from the bar!I do not reccomment visiting the Korean restaurant next door to the hotel!My bf and i visited this for takeout after a night out, clearly they though they could take advantage of us because we had a drink. We ordered soup and plain boiled rice, and the charged us 22 dollars!! when i looked in the bag in the room, they had added extra dishes we didnt want, and obviously the most expensive soup and rice that we didnt want!!I was really angry and took the order back, as soon as the guy saw me he tried to play dumb and said the extra dishes were complimentry before i even said a thing!! Admission of guilt straight away! I then argued that if this was the case then they charged 22 dollars for rice and soup and it was really not acceptable and demanded my cash back, whcih he gave me.Avoid like the plague - there food isnt even that nice!!All in all its a lovely hotel and the majority of staff are pleasant and helpfull, clean and confortable which is whats required after a hard day in NYC. its situated in a great spot, just a few blocks form ESB, times square and macys.i would reccommend this hotel and hopefully will return to stay here again.

<Author>SG3London_UK
<Content>Great Location, helpful and friendly staff, coffee on tap! Just spent six nights at the Hotel Metro, across the New Year period. This was my fifth time in New York and I can honestly say the Metro is the best hotel i've stayed in there so far. We booked a Deluxe non-smoking king room and whilst we didn't get the view of the Empire State building, the room was large by New York standards and the bed as comfortable as ours at home. The hotel is located just a couple of blocks from Macy's, central to everything. We found the hotel staff to be superb, they could not have been more helpful or friendly. Quite unusually for New York the rate included breakfast, basic but more than adequate and the big plus was that coffee/tea were available all day and night in the dining room/lounge just off the lobby, a welcome feature when returning from a day's sightseeing/shopping. The only downside was the unreliability of the lifts, one seemed to be out most days, but this is a small price to pay, for a medium sized(much more personality than a big faceless hotel), clean, centrally located lovely hotel. The other plus was the view of the Empire State from the roof of the hotel (used as a bar in Summer) it was closed due to the freezing conditions, but you could still go up and look at the amazing unobstructed view.

<Author>KathMacca
<Content>A great Christmas in NYC I have just returned from a 6 night trip to NYC over Christmas with my husband. We stayed at the Metro and couldn't fault it one bit. The room was great, clean, surprisingly large and on the 12th floor, so great views of the Empire State Building. Breakfast was great and unlimited as was the tea and coffee. NYC was fantastic and we did all the sights and the highlight was definately the Rockafella Centre both during the day and at night. We treated ourselves to lunch at the Maze Restaurant (at the London Hotel, Gordon Ramsey's place) on Christmas Day which was excellent and then saw Jersey Boys in the evening - both highly recommended. Got some bargains in Macys and you must visit the MMs store! A tip on the shopping front would be to get out there by 9.00/9.30 as by lunchtime the shops and streets are packed.O'Lunneys on 45th street is great for food and if you want something quick the Chinese next door to the hotel is well worth a visit.

<Author>scottme
<Content>Metro highly recommended With my wife and two teenage children I spent five nights at the Metro in one of their family suites a week before Christmas. The rooms are generously sized for central Manhattan, particularly the two-bedded room that the kids had, overlooking 35th St. The beds are comfortable, the bathroom well-supplied with large towels and Gilchrist  Soames toiletries. The free buffet breakfast is limited but perfectly adequate, and the constant free hot drinks were very welcome, particularly when we arrived back after a hard day out. Free WiFi was convenient for researching things to do and for keeping in touch with home.On the downside, the Metro's elevators are small and slow, and one of the pair kept breaking down, leading to long delays at busy times. We also had some problems with the TVs, only getting a few or the many channels we should have had, and the hotel maintenance people were not able to fix this before we left. But we'd not come to NY to watch TV so it was no major issue.The hotel location is excellent, on W35th St between 5th and 6th Avenues. Herald Square subway station is two minutes walk; Macy's is right across 6th Ave (but what a disappointment!) There are lots of shops on 34th St and of course 5th Ave. Times Square is a 10 minute walk, or one stop on the subway. We bought MTA unlimited ride tickets so didn't hestiate to take the subway to get out of the snow and rain! The Empire State Building is a 5 minutes walk away, so we were able to get there early and avoid any queueing to get up to the observation deck, though we found the views from the Top of the Rock at Rockefeller Center equally good.There are plenty of eating options close by. More than once we had a pizza or a slice from Guiseppe's on the corner of 35th and 6th - simple and delicious.The staff were unfailingly friendly and helpful. Nowhere in Manhattan is cheap, but I felt we got our money's worth at the Metro and I'd have no qualms about staying there again.

<Author>Smfarnsworth
<Content>Proof that there are good deals in New York city I've stayed in New York numerous times over the years and can honestly say that the Metro Hotel really does give you value for money.Plus Points: The rooms were clean, moderately sized, we asked for a bathroom (as opposed to a shower) and were given one. The hotel staff were very friendly and helpful - especially on reception and the door. We had a free breakfast in the morning - only toasts and muffins - but it was FREE. We could have tea/coffee whenever we wanted. We weren't bothered by noise - from outside or other guests. It is only 12 floors and I says it has 179 rooms - which is small enough for it to still have a personal touch unlike the gigantic places like the Penn Hotel around the corner.You could walk to Penn Station in about 6 minutes, Macy's in about 2 minutes, Time Square in about 10 minutes and Tiffany's etc in about 20 minutes. There is a subway/tube/underground station less than a minute away and so can be anywhere on the island in no time at all.We got a hotel shuttle back to JFK for $20 each (plus tip) - much cheaper than a taxi $80 (plus tip) and quicker than the Sky Train - to be fair - we would have caught the Sky Train back but there were engineering/track problems near to JFK and didn't want a bus transfer.Negative Points: Not many really - I thought it had free WifI but it didn't, no coffee/tea facilities in the room - but we just brought coffee to the room, the coffee wasn't the nicest in the world, the hanging space isn't the largest in the world and the radiator worked fine but it was a dry heat (fan assisted) which wasn't overly comfortable. These are only very minor points though - and compared with some HOLES like the Penn Hotel this was luxurious and we would definitely go back again.Also, the restaurant attached to the hotel isn't great - if you are tired and it's raining and don't want to go out - the food is passable - but I would really force yourself further afield - even if it's only to cross the road to the Bar  Grill

<Author>Junglejuice30
<Content>Can't beat the Hotel Metro! We booked for a four night stay at the Hotel Metro in November 2008 through Thomson Signature. The hotel had been recommended to us by some friends who had previously stayed there. We had originally booked for a deluxe double but the room we had been allocated, although perfectly roomy and clean, smelled of smoke. George on Reception was our hero and very kindly upgraded us to a Family Suite! One bedroom window had a view of the Empire State Building and the other bedroom window had a view of Macys! What more could we ask for?! The room was spotlessly clean with the most comfortable bed I've ever slept in. Coffee and tea were available 24 hours a day downstairs and the breakfast was fantastic - bagels over here are not a patch on the real thing!Location-wise, you couldn't get much better if you tried. 1 block from the Empire State Building, a block from Macy's, 5th Avenue and all its shops are right on your doorstep. The Reception staff that we had contact with were all extremely helpful, gave advice and suggestions on where to go, what to see and the best/cheapest way of doing it. Again, a big shout out to George!There is a small gym on the top floor of the hotel, next to the roof terrace. I did go with the best intentions but never got round to using it - pounding the streets of New York was exercise enough!All in all, it was a fantastic and we are planning our return trip for next year to the same hotel.

<Author>Lucyboom
<Content>An okay but expensive hotel let down by lazy front desk staff We stayed for nine nights from 14 November, on arrival there was no one to help with our luggage, so we struggled into the hotel (upstairs) with our bags and were told the hotel had no real views of the Empire State Building, but we had been upgraded from a double to a king size room (room 711), which we did appreciate, the view from this room was a building site, which began work at 8am everyday, however. The bed was large and amazingly comfortable, linen soft and the room was very well serviced on a daily basis. My only gripe about the bed would have to be the use of a quilt instead of blankets, this seems to be a trend in hotels these days, it isn't good and there is obviously no way of adjusting the layers as there is with blankets, the quilt was covered with a nasty nylon cover which we removed on our first night as it was too hot and felt horrid.There was no bath, which I did miss being a bath lover and find it especially useful after a long day on my feet. The fridge was one of those 'if you remove anything for more than 20 seconds you will be charged' mechanisms, and it was not possible to store anything of our own in there, and the mini bar was the same. So don't pick those USD6 MMs up for too long or you'll pay for them. There was an ice bucket in the room and an ice machine on level 12, which we used to store our drinks. The hotel supplied free tea (bags) and filtered coffee and fresh milk, in the breakfast room all day and night, which was very nice. Breakfast itself was carbohydrate city, about five different kinds of bagels, muffins, sugary cereal and bread, with babybel cheese, cream cheese, peanut butter, grape jelly and orange marmalade. 'Juices' from concentrates and some instant oatmeal. I would have appreciated a low fat protein option, or even some boiled eggs, and given it is not a cheap hotel I think not an unreasonable expectation.I had three parcels arrive for me whilst at was at the hotel, on each occasion I was not told of their arrival and had to ask, the third one, when I did ask, I was told had not arrived. After messing about contacting the sender and her telling me it had been signed for by the hotel staff, three days earlier, I went back to the front desk who finally got off their backsides and found it. In ever other decent hotel I've stayed in, any packages have been delivered straight to my room, no questions asked. In addition we paid USD80 to have laundry done, which we also had to collect from the front desk. (are the staff glued to their chairs??)The wifi internet access to the rooms is almost non-existent and drops out every five minutes or so, my partner was attempting to work from our room one day and ended up having to go to the business centre. When he was unable to connect at all at one stage, the front desk staff just gave him the number of their wifi supplier and told him to phone them, and then tried to charge us for the phone call!! (A friend of ours was also staying in the hotel on the 9th floor, he too had trouble with bad wifi connection, so it wasn't just our room or floor). The cordless phone in the room had terrible reception and would drop out for every other word, we didn't use it much but when we did it was truly terrible.Overall, an okay hotel, with a subway nearby and Macy's just one block away, however, the front desk staff are lazy and unhelpful and really let the hotel down. I am not sure if I would stay here again, I suspect there are better hotels in the same price range.  
<Date>Nov 26, 2008

<Author>jovi19
<Content>Superb, want to go back asap Just come back from the Metro, travelled with my Daughter and a friend to celebrate my Daughters 18th birthday. I had already contacted concierge in advance to arrange a few birthday surprises and had absolutely no complaints, everything was organised, the cost was cheaper than I could have found it and the pre arrival service faultless.On arrival we were delighted to have been upgraded. Our room was spotless and roomy, we sneaked a look at some other rooms and again although smaller, would have had no complaints.Bell hops, particularly Matthew were lovely and really funny, nothing was to much trouble. Ann on reception and the other man on the desk (I forgot his name) deserve a mention and credit for a really good job. I do know which receptionist people are mentioning, and yes she isn't the friendliest of characters and could do with a happy pill perhaps, but hey we all have bad days and perhaps she has more than others.The breakfast was lovely and just enough to fire you up for the day. Coffee and tea on tap 24/7 was an additional bonus. The hotel bar was expensive (but to be honest in the current financial climate the whole of New York is). Having read reviews before we left I was unsure just what to expect, it would go one way or the other. I can honestly say the entire stay was faultless, yes there is a little noise but tell me who expects to go to New York and find peace and quiet? Its all part of the experience.Location was perfect, ignore the bus ticket sellers (red  Yellow jackets) go via yellow cab, far cheaper in the long run and quicker. If you are out late at night the bus stops at 6.30 anyway, so you would have to take a cab.Get to the Empire State Building as it opens at 8am and avoid the queues we were up at the top enjoying the views ... and snow at 8.06am!! We had been awake since 5 as the jet lag was kicking in so the early start wasn't a problem.The other thing to be aware of and something that did unnerve us was that we were 'given' promotional cd's outside Virgin megastore. They were signed by 'friendly' enough guys who, we assumed were promoting their music and were legitimate given where they were standing!. They then made it clear that they wanted money and were not going to take no for an answer, surrounding us at one point and it was quite scary. We did get away without paying, but please, if approached ignore and do not accept anything they try to give youBack to the hotel, would recommend to anyone, I have stayed in hotels all over the place some basic, some 5 star this was BY FAR the best ever and hope to get back there as soon as my credit card and the exchange rate have recovered!!.

<Author>Mariafromnz
<Content>Very Average for the price! I know this is New York and that what you get for your money isn't the same value as you pay and receive in other parts of the country, but this would not be my first choice ever again! Yes, it's conveniently located, right in between 5th and 6th Avenue, and yes, the rooms aren't too badly sized for New York. But, why wouldn't I stay there again? Firstly, there's no room service - well, there is, but the menu is limited and you can't charge it to your room! When I questioned this, I got a very terse response from the person on the phone, suggesting that I was strange to expect that kind of service! There weren't coffee making facilities in the room and we couldn't even get any brought up in the morning- not that this is a huge deal, but it's appreciated when you can do this. Secondly, the breakfast was ok, and included in the price, which is great -but it's all on plastic, disposable plates and cutlery - easy on the clean-up for them but not so great given environmental concerns. Thirdly, when we arrived into our room the carpet was more than damp and smelt very strongly of cleaning product. Great that the floor had been cleaned but it was horrible walking around on the carpet!! Finally, the beds were so incredibly hard that I left feeling like my body had been beaten to a pulp - and I had just 2 nights there! Hate to think what would have happened if I'd been there longer! On the good side though, the doorman we had was great - friendly, which is odd for NYC, and happily stored our bags for us and then made sure our taxi was there to take us to the airport when we needed it to. He didn't openly ask for a tip, as I have had other hotel staff do in the past, but we were happy to offer him one just for being so friendly and helpful! So, for the price we paid, no I wouldn't recommend it -you'd be better off at the Courtyard by Marriot!

<Author>football_lily
<Content>Fantastic location We stayed here for 3 nights from 30 September. We booked through BA who had a more favourable rate than other websites or the hotel direct.The hotel has a fantastic location, only 2 mins walk from a subway station and Macy's, and has views of the Empire State Building. The central location does mean that the rooms suffer from street noise due to a lack of double glazing, but you get used to it.The complimentary breakfast is a real bonus, and there is a plentiful selection of rolls, muffins, bagels, fruit, yoghurt etc. However, the breakfast area is not big enough to accommodate everyone at busy times, and it turns into a bit of a free for all!Staff were friendly and helpful, and we were able to check in early on arrival. The concierge was very helpful with looking after our bags on our last day, and arranging a taxi for us.The room was comfortable and very clean, and the hotel offers free wi-fi access which we found very useful.Overall a very enjoyable stay. This was our 4th visit to NY, and the Metro offered excellent value for money compared with other hotels we have stayed at. We we would definitely stay here again if we return.

<Author>mike8696
<Content>stay here just for the view on roof terrace Hotel Metro - New York - 45 West 35th StreetJust got back to England after a weekend break staying at the Hotel Metro with my 19yr old son, this hotel is fantastic. if it's in your price budget DO NOT hesitate.Compared to similar priced Hotels i think this is the one to stay at. Only 12 floors, which by New York standards, makes it quiet and never any queues at reception or for breakfast etc.I cannot think of a better location, next street to Empire State Building, Macy's next block, Lovely clean Hotel, DON'T believe any bad reviews here, i justthink some people would complain at anything they probably blame the hotel if it rains!! Also it is exactly how it looks in the gallery pictures as it's recently been renovated. All Staff were fantastic, rooms lovely, we booked a Queen room, but got upgraded to a Suite (room1102) free of charge.Highlight is the roof bar/terrace, just awesome view of the ESB,watching people's faces when they first look up on arrival to the terrace for the first time is priceless.Continental breakfast was a great start to the day (i understand most hotels don't provide it free within the price) and as much coffee as you can drink all day  night. Because of the jet lag, i woke up at 3am, decided to go down to breakfast room, grab a coffee and back up onto roof terrace. just to sit and take it all in.PS. Tip for any visitor to New York, visit 'Top of the Rock' at the Rockerfeller centre, the view over Manhattan and Central Park is breathtaking, and the bonus over the Empire State Building, is that you get to see it in the view.Mike  Greg WeatherheadAlcester, England

<Author>Kathy009
<Content>Great find Have just arrived back from a week at the Hotel Metro, New York. Having read some negative reviews on this site before we booked we were delighted we had ignored them. From the minute we arrived at Reception the staff were unfailingly welcoming and helpful. The room was an adequate size bearing in mind this was New York and the bathroom had recently been updated with a super large shower cubicle. Good quality toiletries were very welcome as we had travelled hand luggage only. Our window looked out at the Empire State Building which was illuminated at night. Breakfast of fresh fruit, yoghourt, cheese, muffins and various pastries plus toast set us up for the day and hot drinks available all day were a lovely bonus when we arrived back from a hard day sightseeing. We used to take it to our room and collapse on the bed. Free wireless access and two computers were a bonus. Great roof garden was lovely but the food was spoiled by having to be brought up from the restaurant on the ground floor on cold plates so food cold and all drinks including wine served in plastic glasses. The situation couldn't be better right in the middle of Manhattan with a subway station 50 yards away. Pizza place on the corner was great for a snack but was not impressed with Brendons across the road. Bryant Park on 42nd Street is a great place for a rest if in the neighbourhood. Tables, chairs, free newspapers,books and games of chess. With hand luggage it is easy to get to the hotel by air train/subway. We got there quicker than some other people who had taken a taxi.

<Author>EllieManchester
<Content>Superb location This hotel was recommended to me by a friend, and we got a good deal by paying in advance on ba.com.The hotel's website makes it out to be posher than it actually is, but in terms of location it's superb - virtually opposite Macy's (I was there for shopping after all), very near Empire State Building and a very short walk from Times Square/5th avenue. We hardly took the subway at all. We got a deluxe room which was old fashioned but very spacious - only slight niggle was that the air con was noisy but this is typical of older hotels. Staff were not terribly friendly, and I was disappointed not to be able to get into my room until 5pm on the first day, despite my voucher stating clearly that check in was from 3pm.Breakfast is interesting, nice continental offering but served on the kind of plastic plate you would expect at a children's party. However most hotels in new york don't offer breakfast at all! Nice touch is that tea and coffee is available all day in the lounge. On the top floor there was a lovely open air bar, very pleasant on a warm evening. Not the best hotel I've ever stayed in by a long way, but great location if you can get a good deal.

<Author>destinationqueen
<Content>Please read if you plan on staying here When we arrived at Hotel Metro, we were pleasantly surprised with the 1950's decor, and the smell of cleaning supplies. We booked a double bed suite which was beautiful and spacious. There was a large bay window that looked out onto the street below. Everything was great, until the next morning when I awoke to two bed bugs in my bed, and a fresh wound on my leg. I took the comforter off my bed and the other one, and found one more bug in the other bed. I went down to the concierge and alerted them of this issue, and they nonchalantly said that they would switch us to a different room. I was a little shocked by this behavior, since no sympathy was shown, and no manager came out to offer their apologies. I packed everything up, and brought it downstairs (they said the new room wouldn't be ready until 3pm). When I returned later in the day, I asked the concierge if they would be able to dry our clothes - since there were bed bugs, I didn't want to risk moving them from room to room and possibly being bitten again. I was told that they don't do that. Again, I was shocked at the lack of customer service. I asked someone else, and they gave me a name of a cleaner 4 blocks away - I was told to bring the receipt back for the manager to review for a refund. So I dragged two suitcases full of clothes 4 blocks, just to find out that the cleaners don't just dry clothes that they are a full service cleaner with a two-day turn around time - even though we told them the hotel had sent us. So I hauled the clothes back to the hotel and told the concierge what happened (I had asked to speak to a manager, but was told that he had gone home).Then someone else stepped in and said that house-keeping would do it. Now why couldn't this have been done in the first place??When we arrived at our new room, we were sorely disappointed. The room was significantly smaller than the first one we had(although, later, the manager assured us that it was the exact same type of room). The blinds looked like someone had torn them down, crushed them, and hung them back up and the wallpaper in the bathroom was peeling and was held on in one corner with several pushpins. We decided to just deal with the room conditions, since we didn't want to have to move again. Our laundry was dried and delivered to our room.The next morning, I went down and asked to speak with the manager. I told him everything that had happened, and he simply answered with I am aware of the situation, but then proceeded to tell me that the bugs that were found in the bed were not bed bugs. It wasn't until after several times of me saying how disappointed I was in the level of customer service, that he finally offered his apologies. He said he would speak with his general manager to see what he could do. Later, he left a message informing me that one night of our stay would be removed from the bill.This was a very generous offer, and I am thankful, but I am still appalled at the way the whole situation was handled, it was like pulling teeth just to get someone to say they were sorry for our inconvenience.

<Author>LondonFlybynight
<Content>Good Location and a little different Cheapest place by far to book this hotel is through the BA Website.This hotel is in a great location and only one block from the Empire State Building and two minutes from Maceys. We have just spent three nights there and found the Art Deco styling a pleasant change from the normal US hotel rooms. The continental breakfast is good with a choice of cereal, muffins, begels, toast, yogurt and fruit. Free tea and coffee are served all day which was a nice touch (although it meant no in-room facilities).The staff were efficient and polite although not over friendly apart from the doorman Mathew who was always smiling and very helpful. If you like Chineses food the restaraunt a couple of doors along is reasonable and frequented predominently by oriental patrons (it's the one that does display the prices and is nearest to the hotel)New York is always noisy but be aware that there is some construction work going on adjacent to the hotel which will impact on your rest if you want a lie in, we were up by 06:30 and out fairly swiftly so were not affected.Finally, skip the trip to the top of the Empire state building and go to the Rockerfeller building (Top of the Rock) after dark and enjoy a far better view, and you get to see the Empire State Building all lit up.

<Author>carebear42
<Content>Great Hotel, Close to everything We stayed at this hotel for three nights in June and thought this hotel was fantastic. The room was small compared to what we were used from the rest of out trip but had everything we needed. The free breakfast supplied in the morning was fantastic and just what you needed before a long day walking around NY. This hotel is has a subway entrance just near by which can get you to just about anywhere.Penn Station is within walking distance which is great if you arrive in NY by train (as we did). Macy's is on the corner and the 5th Ave is only a block away for some great shopping. The Empire State Building is just around the corner. We found the staff helpful and polite. We made the mistake of spending our other 3 nights in NY at another hotel to reduce the cost, but wished we hadn as the Metro hotel was fantastic. I would recommend this hotel to anyone who is looking for a comfortable place to sleep when exploring the Big Apple.

<Content>Great Hotel in good location We spent 4 nights at this great hotel - the staff were very helpful and the breakfasts very nice - cereals,bagels,fruit and muffins. <Author>Buff_G
<Content>great little hotel in the heart of midtown My boyfriend and I stayed at this hotel from June 21st through to June 24th for a 4 night break in NY that we booked via Virgin Holidays as part of a package deal.I had pre-requested a room in the quietest part of the hotel as i am such a light sleeper. We were allocated room 701 on the 7th Floor. I am not sure if the room we had was any quieter than the others but at 7.30am each morning we were woken up but what sounded like rubbish trucks collecting rubbish for half hour each day! Also we alwyas heard loud police/ ambulence/ fire truck sirens each night but that was no big deal as they came and went quickly (and in NY i guess thsi is the norm anyway).The staff at the hotel are great. nothing is too much trouble and they are great at giving directions. they all seems to know the local areas well.The breakfast at the hotel is brilliant. bagels/ muffins/ pastries/ cereals/ tea/ coofee/ juice/ fruit and yoghurt was on offer every morning and never ran out no matter what time we went. It's on from 6.30 - 11.00 am in the hotel dining area. there was always a table for us to use however i am sure it would have been a little trickier if there had been a bigger group of us.The room we had was very small but it was so clean and had a lovely powershower and comfy bed so the size of the room didn't make any difference. We had a one bedded double delux room.From the hotel we walked to Port Authority - 15 mins- Central Park - 30 mins - 5th Ave main shops 15mins - Times Square - 10 mins - Herald Square 5 mins. everything taht is a major attraction in midtown is within and easy wlaking distance!All in all i would definately stay at this hotel again and highly reccomend it.

<Author>Canadian67
<Content>Great room, clean, but some problems We stayed at the Metro for five days. We chose it because of its location and because of the availability of familiy suites which give our adult son his own room in which to thrash about.Both our bedroom and our son's were very large and comfortable and clean. The bathroom was also large and clean. The location (midtown) is excellent and public transportation readily available. The breakfasts were ample, diverse, and well-stocked.However, there were several aspects of the stay which, minor in themselves, showed some significant management problems.We arrived early, around 12 noon, and left our baggage in a locked room while the harried staff doubted our room would be ready before four o'clock which they claimed was check-in time. The website was clear that three o'clock was check-in but they chose to argue with me about it and, worse, when we came back around three they had made no effort to have our room cleaned even though they knew we would be back. Finally around 3:30 we were permitted to take possession of our room where their own printed guide to services spoke of a three o'clock check-in.There are only two elevators available for guests which made for a very tight fit in the morning period. We were on the ninth floor and many who try to get on at 3, 4, or 5 were forced to wait for another.The toilet leaked quite noisily and a call to the front desk did not resolve the problem which we lived with by keeping the doors shut.There is an extra breakfast room down a hallway but no one on their staff bothers to tell you about it and we often had to tell other guests that it was okay to sit there because it was unclear that we could. Certainly it was barren of any other niceties such as flowers on the table that were in the main breakfast room and chairs were stacked on tables like we were unexpected end unwelcome.For some reason my son's bedroom had no door. It seems likely that this was originally designed as a one-bedroom suite but as they now call it a two-bedroom family suite it ought to have had a door.Despite all these problems (which we did not allow to ruin our stay) we were generally pleased with the location, cleanliness, and size but the management needs to attend to these sorts of problems.

<Author>Wincey
<Content>Great service and location! Excellent stay at the Metro - ideal location for the first time visitor. Loved the roof top terrace and the view from our window of the Empire State. The photos on the hotel website do it justice.Breakfast ok considering included in price - lots of bagels, muffins, bread, cereal etc.Very hot weather when we were there and we had to have the air con on constantly which was a little noisy - but then so is NYC!Subway within very short distance. If you feel like splashing out go to the Rainbow Grill in the Rockerfeller Centre for a champagne cocktail and relish the lovely evening views.

<Content>Location and, um, pillows! Bagels, cereal, fresh fruit salad, coffee, toast, juice...I highly recommend the Metro. If you are susceptible to noise, ask for an interior room. <Content>Right up my street... We selected the Metro as it was offered with a really good rate from the BA website when booking flights for this, our third NYC trip + it had some really good reviews on here, and I have to say we would go back to the Metro again based on this visit.The location was great being so close to 34th St Subway, a block away from Macy's  from ESB, and walking distance from Times Square etc.We really liked the rooftop bar, and the breakfast was just what we needed. <Content>OK stay at the Hotel Metro We stayed at the Hotel Metro for 5 nights. The hotel was very clean and enjoyed the continental breakfasts. The Hotel was in easy walking distance to Times Square, the Flat Iron Building, Macys, Madison Square Gardens, Central Station and it was not too far to Central Park (we did it in about 25 minutes). The reception staff were always helpful but when we arrived we were told booking in was not until 4.00 p.m. so we had to go for a walk about until it was 4.00. I would stay at this hotel again but would ask for a room on the back of the hotel next time or take my ear plugs again!

<Author>maritou
<Content>Great spot in the middle of NYC Just came back from NYC. Went for weekend with a friend (in her 50's) and my boyfriend (both in our early 30's). It was our 5th time in the Big Apple. Drove there and parked the car at a Parking lot in the same block of the Hotel Metro. We stayed for 2 nights in the hotel family suite. Great staff, friendly. Room is a double room with one shared bathroom. One room is smaller with a door for more privacy, nice queen size bed and tv, 2 windows, small desk. Second room is a very large one with 2 double beds, tv, with a small table and nice cozy chair in a corner, one window. Everything was very clean. The bathroom is decent size, well equipped but bath is old and not emptying very fast....that is the only thing we did not like. Wireless internet working great. The breakfast is included , very yummy and runs until 11ham wich is great for people who do not like to get up too early. The roof terrace is real nice, with amazing view of the Empire State Building, great place to relax after a long day walking around NYC. Even if you are in the middle of Manhattan, the rooms are fairly quiet(you can hear once in a while a louder street noise but nothing to wake you up from your sleep). The 3 of us would definitely go back, price is worth it (we paid total of 960$ for 2 nights taxes inc. (Saturday and Sunday)Plus 50$ for parking for 48hours.) You could sleep comfortably 4 people or even 3 couples if you don't mind sharing one bathroom and if the hotel rules let you do that...not sure. I am glad we stayed there, it is a great choice for people who do not mind a little less luxury and a little more room. Pictures from hotel website can be trusted.

<Author>kristihart
<Content>Great Hotel, Great Location! We just returned from our stay at the Hotel Metro, and were very pleased! We booked our room through Hotels.com, which usually gets you a smaller room with a double bed. However upon arrival, the friendly staff upgraded our room to the larger queen room in the back of the hotel, without us even asking! They were great at recommending restaurants and activities for our stay, and were overall very nice! The room was a good size, with good amenities within, and great toiletries. The bathroom is definitely on the small side, which made for interesting showers, as there really isn't anywhere to put your shampoo, conditioner, etc while in the shower! It wasn't a big problem though, as the rest of the room was just great. The breakfast is a major plus- it saved us a lot of money throughout our stay! There were yummy bagels, muffins, cinnamon toast, cereal, fruit,  juice. The breakfast goes until 11am, which works out great for those late mornings after a long night exploring! The rooftop deck offers a great view of the Empire State Building, which is a must-see. Another plus is the great location. We stayed here based off everyone's reviews about the great location, and were definitely pleased! There are subways literally steps away, which works out great. Macy's is very close, and the ESB is just around the corner! The pizza place on the corner like the other reviewer mentioned is a great place for a slice of pizza! The Hotel is on 35th st between 5th and 6th avenues, which makes it a little less loud than being, say, in times square, but offers enough traffic so you can easily catch a cab during the day. Overall, the location is definitely a major advantage, with it being close enough to everything you need and easy to navigate from! We really enjoyed our stay at the Hotel Metro, and as a first-time visitor to New York City, found the staff to be very helpful, and would highly recommend it!

<Author>flyinmom
<Content>Shhh, don't tell anyone how good this is, we'll never get back in!!! Apparently, this hotel used to be a bit tacky and run down. Well, evidently they have undergone some fairly recent renos, because this turned out to be a fantastic little find; a real gem of a hotel. You can beat the location, 35th and 6th, a subway stop right at the end of the street, walking distance to much, a block away from the Empire State Bldg., and only really ever a 10-15 minute cab or subway ride to anywhere else. We loved it!We had a family of 4 in one of their family rooms. We booked online direct with them. My sister had a separate room; she booked through Expedia. The ouble?room she got is not advertised on the Hotel own site; those rooms are just a bit smaller and they reserve those for companies like Expedia to use. The front desk staff and doorman are all great and helpful; evidently there for a while, and when a hotel in NYC can keep its staff loyal like that, it tells me something. All the room cleaning staff were wearing back supports to protect them; that tells me the hotel cares enough to ensure their on the job safety.Our room, 902, was toward the back of the hotel, which is good, because it was very quiet. My sister original room, 203, was a the top of the stairs from the lobby. The first night, she got no sleep due to the noise level; the sound really carries up from the lobby, so if youe a light sleeper, pass on that room. There also a place under construction right next door, and they have an overnight shift that is working it that also contributed to the noise factor. However, the next day, the hotel very graciously, and without any fuss, agreed to move my sister. She ended up in 712, a slightly larger accommodation, and it was much better. Note that all the -08 rooms are immediately across from the elevator doors, so light sleepers will hear that traffic all night.The family room is a 3 bed accommodation, one master queen bedroom, the other 2 double beds in an open room. It really does look just like the pictures on the web. Both rooms had TVs, good sized single bathroom and shower, and a separate 2nd sink outside. In room mini bar, but read the rules about that carefully. Nice selection of amenities in the bathroom. The carpets are evidently fairly new. The towels were all close to pa?quality; not one worn towel in the bunch for 5 days. They have a lounge off the lobby which is where you can get all day coffee/tea, and where brekkie is served. We were actually quite surprised by the quality and quantity of the breakfast foods. Fresh bagels and huge muffins, fresh fruit, fruit salad, yogurts, all manner of toasts, including pop tarts (!) and cereal. It tends to get a bit crowded in there around 8:30 but by 9:00, it opens up again. TVs and complimentary newspapers throughout.Next to the location, the best part of the Hotel Metro was the price. We had originally made our reservation at the Affinia Manhattan, because it was often recommended on TA, but they were charging $700+ for their 2 bedroom suite, which includes a kitchenette, but no breakfast, and it was right near the train station. Metro charged $423, including breakfast, and it a 4 minute walk to Macy. The room was huge, and all in all we were totally delighted with the place. We'd go back in a heartbeat!

<Author>SiteJanny
<Content>Perfect Central Location We've just arrived back from a great long weekend in Manhatten, staying at the Hotel Metro and wanted to share our experience with others thinking of this Hotel as an option.We selected the Metro because of its apparent central position, and we weren't disappointed. Flying Continental into Newark, we'd picked a direct flight out, returning to Edinburgh via Birmingham so we could steer clear of the mess at Heathrow. Continental looked after us pretty well. The flight took 7 and a half hours, departing and arriving on time. Their choice of in-flight entertainment was very impressive and made the journey more bearable. Arriving at Newark, we took the New Jersey Transit train from Newark into New York Penn Station, only three blocks from the Metro. Two adult and one child on the train cost only $33 each way. Cheaper than a cab, and we were at Penn Station 40 minutes after boarding the train. The Metro sits in a narrow street only a block away from both the Empire State Building (left) and Macy's (right), so its already a good starting point for sightseeing. It isn't a big hotel but we found it very comfortable for our needs. Listen, you don't visit New York City to sit around a hotel room all day ! ! ! Get out there and enjoy the place ! Our party of three had booked into a Double Double room. We expected abit of a squeeze for 4 days. When we arrived we were delighted to find that they'd allocated us something akin to a small suite - one main bedroom with two double beds, one separate room with another double bed, and a shower room. Power shower would be an understatement ! Oh, and my 'other half' complained that the hairdryer lacked any power to actually dry her hair. CRISIS ! There was a well-stocked fridge with plenty of choice although the prices were typical hotel prices, with a curious warning that any item removed for more than 20 seconds would be billed to you... HOW WOULD THEY KNOW??? Was Big Brother watching???Heeding warnings we'd read about street noise, our 3rd floor room proved low enough to benefit from the full flavour of the neighbouring Irish Bars, and the 24hr horn-honking that is the staple diet of US drivers. But it only disturbed us on the first night. Every other night, we were so tired from walking and the fresh air, that we slept like babies. Breakfast was included in our price but to be honest, was our only disappointment. You have to get in and out early to beat the crush. The layout of the continental style servery is poor as it occupies a corner of the dining room. This means that if its busy, you get trapped by the mass waiting behind you. There's no 'flow'. There's also a lack of seating so that on two of our four mornings, I had to stand beside the table as my family ate, failing miserably in my attempt to eat a large bagel gracefully ! !Service is very good. Staff are polite, helpful and attentive without being in your face. For example - When my partner asked ME to ask the lone female on reception where we could find Hooters (she wanted one of their T-Shirts !) the receptionist didn't even bat an eye as she checked the internet details, called them to check their address, then gave me written details to locate them !Incidentally, I didn't taste any of the Hooters fried chicken I ordered - I was too busy ogling the waitress ! !The main bus tour companies operate past the Empire State, so arranging and buying tickets was easy and well worth the cost. We could get on or off anywhere on their route at any time from 9am til 6pm and their tour guides were both informative and amusing. For us, it was all about location though. Times Square is 10 minutes walk away from the Metro. Penn Station is also home to Madison Square Garden - again a 10 minute walk. The Empire State sits on 5th Avenue, renowned for its shopping. And Broadway is at the end of the street so the theatres begin 5 minutes walk away.Would we go back? In a heartbeat. Would we stay at the Metro again? Definitely.Would we take the family again? Absolutely... not ! Next time, we're going by ourselves so that we can enjoy more of the evening entertainment and we won't have to visit MM world again ! ! !One word of warning. Prepare to leave your manners and courtesy behind you. This is a big city. It seemed like everyone was fixated on where they were going, and anything between them and their destination was game for being barged out of the way, without apolgy or even acknowledgment. It won't spoil your enjoyment of this fabulous place though. Enjoy.

<Author>handyspanner
<Content>What can you add!!! We stayed at the Metro during the first week of April, taking a vacation and a shopping trip for the better half. Well, there can not be a lot to add to all the previously positive comments, only to say that I agree totally and the hotel is a great find for NY. For what you pay and what you get, with the room, hotel and staff, it is exceptional value and we will definitely stay there again.The hotel is located in a great position between 5th and 6th Avenue and is easy to access from Newark Airport. We caught the train from the airport to NY Penn, which took about 30 minutes and cost $15, then walked for 10 minutes to the hotel from the station. The walk is easy and on the way you pass the shops and Madison Square Gardens, if it a sunny day you also get a great initial view of the ESB! The hotel is five minutes from Macy's one way and five minutes from the shops of 5th Avenue the other. It takes about 10 - 15 minutes to walk to Times Square and subway access is just at the end of the street.While we were there we saw two shows on Broadway and purchased the tickets for $60 a piece from the last minute booth on 46th Street, just behind the Marriot off the Times Square area.I would also recommend the restaurant across the road from the Hotel, Brendan, as on the first night we walked for ages looking for a place to eat and ended back here. The atmosphere was good and so was the food and value. There is a great selection of fish and meat and the staff are really helpful. Try it; it is a good place for the first night, until you get your bearings.The Statton Island ferry was good too, and you get great views of DT Manhattan.If you do happen to go to Macey's get your discount card from the visitors centre on the ground floor mezzanine level, you will save 11% on most of your purchases and should provide a slight relief to the credit card!!Enjoy.  
<Date>Apr 12, 2008

<Author>emilymce
<Content>Great experience overall We stayed in the hotel at the end of February for a week and I have to say it's great! The reason I chose it was because of the reviews I'd read here- so I just wanted to add my compliments.Firstly, the best thing about this hotel is location, location, location. This was our first time in NYC, so we were really booking blind. It's within walking distance to most of the sights, and for those places a bit far away, there's a subway station less than a minute away. Macy's is a stone's throw away, and the Empire State Building is just around the corner- though you can see it from your room if you're feeling lazy!Most of the staff were lovely, and very helpful with booking tours and giving advice and directions.The breakfast is amazing- about 5 different types of bagels, breads, cheeses, fruit, cereal, muffins, juices, tea, coffee- it was really a great set up for the day. AND there's complimentary coffee and tea in the lobby throughout the day- fantastic!The rooms was lovely too, and really quite big for a standard room. And the safe was really big, our laptop fit in with plenty of room for money, jewellery etc. There's an ipod dock, which is great for listening to some tunes when you're recovering from the days trekking! The shower was gorgeous too- really powerful!And there's plenty of shelf room in the bathroom, which is important for when you're trying to pamper or do make-up! I didn't bother bringing my hairdryer because of space, but the one in the hotel was fine- the battery didn't power out once while I was using it, which can be really annoying in hotels.There was a slight problem with the restaurant- myself and my boyfriend ate there about an hour before they were due to close on a Wednesday, and the food looked like it was thrown together. The waiter was very friendly, but it looked, and tasted, like the food was just taken out of the fridge and popped into the microwave. But I think this business is separate to the hotel- just thought I'd mention it.Basically, I would most definitely book this hotel- it's a real gem. I've compared experiences with other people, and it really seems that for the price we paid, we got so many extras

<Author>misseattle
<Content>Good Location, Small Rooms This reminded me of several independent hotels I've stayed at in Europe. Small rooms, small bathrooms, small elevators...not at all like your American mega-chains. Nothing special about the rooms at all, just your basic and in need of major refurbishing. TV's were very old, with two remotes for different control functions. If you are going to shop in the area--be prepared for large crowds and extremely messing/unorganized racks!! You can tell a million people pass through these shops a day. It was hard to find something that wasn't on the right rack or on the floor.

<Content>Great hotel, great location Excellent hotel. We've just come back from a stay (11-17 March 2008) and I can only reiterate what other positive reviewers have said. A brilliant location, with the 34th St subway 100 yards away which takes you up or down-town to most of the major places in Manhattan. The hotel is incredibly clean and is decorated in a nice modern/1930s style. Our room was at the back of the hotel so quite dark, but with the darkness you also get quiet, away from the hub-bub of Midtown Manhattan, which was much needed after a hectic day in the city. It was spacious and the bed was huge and very comfortable. No tea/coffee making facilities in room but 24 hour access to hot drinks in the downstairs lounge. The staff were very helpful and friendly. Our toilet flooded at one point and a member of the staff came to fix it within minutes. They also provide useful local information. As well as a free breakfast (quite unusual in NYC hotels) there was also free computer access, a gym and an amazing roof terrace which looks out onto the Empire State Building. I would not hesitate to recommend this hotel and will definitely stay there if we go to NYC again. I will be recommending it to all my friends and family!  
<Date>Mar 19, 2008

<Author>Emma1975
<Content>Great location! My mum and I stayed at Hotel Metro in February this year. We received decent rates on Expedia and we were impressed by the reviews the hotel had received on this website.I had booked a month or so in advance and had requested a non-smoking rooms away from the elevator. Much to my disatisfaction, we were given a smoking room right next to the elevator - not impressed! However, in the hotel's defence, the smoking rooms were very well maintained and the smell of smoke was not too bad, it was just when you entered the floor and caught the smoke from the other rooms. Be sure when requesting a non-smoking rooms that it is for health reasons, this will give you a better chance of getting one.The elevator was a bit annoying, hearing people getting in and out all night and the ding as it arrived at our floor. I think our room was one of the older ones, the heater didn't work and there was no in-room safe as their website stated.On a positive note though, the location was sensational! The rooms were very comfortable and always clean. The breakfast each day was great, coffee on tap 24/7 was also a nice treat as both my mum and I are big coffee drinkers. I liked that the hotel had both elevators and stairs for those who don't like elevators. The bell staff could have been a little more helpful. Upon leaving the bell guy watched as my mum and I struggled with our bags, didn't even open the door for us. I found this a little rude.

<Author>amtmcm
<Content>Couldn't Have Been Happier! We stayed in a 2 bedroom suite and found the price to be very reasonable, the room was spacious and we thoroughly enjoyed our visit! The main room had two double beds, a round dining table for 4 and a typical armoire with TV, etc... Nothing fancy, but it was updated, clean and plenty of room to move around. The 2nd bedroom had a king bed, desk and TV stand. It was great to put the kids to bed and be able to retreat to our own space and could watch TV without disturbing them. Breakfast is included downstairs in a very comfortable lounge area made up of 3 rooms with a variety of seating at dining tables or overstuffed armchairs and couches. CNN is on the flat screen TV's and the cold breakfast was generous. There were yogurts, muffins, donuts, toast, bagels, fresh fruit, juice, coffee, tea, hot chocolate, and more. Most guests were European and it was fun to sit and guess what languages were being spoken. There is also a bar upstairs which is open during nice weather with a gorgeous view of the Empire State Building.The staff were all very friendly and helpful and the location was ideal! We were 1/2 a block from Macy's and maybe 3 blocks from the Empire State Building. It would probably be a great location for Madison Square Garden or Bryant Park visitors. There was a subway entrance very close and a Duane Reade drugstore around the corner. Great location, great service, excellent accommodations! We would definitely stay here again!

<Author>Lee123Surrey
<Content>Could not fault it! We booked this hotel on the BA website and was attracted by the price. We were not expecting much but were really suprised and pleased. The reception staff were friendly and even though we checked in early they had our room ready and had left a small gift as they knew it was my birthday. Some have commented on the size of the rooms but there was more then enough space. A queen bed, dressing table, a set of drawers, 2 bed side cabinets and a wardrobe big enough for clothes and 2 suitcases! The free safe is inside the wardrobe - which we had trouble working but someone arrived within 10 minutes to help! The view of the ESB from the roof top terrace was great. The hotel is in a great location, really central and close to Times Square. The sub-way is less then a minute from the hotel and a great way to get about. The breakfast was right up my street and certainly enough to keep you going to lunch, huge muffins, toast, bagels, cereal, fresh fruit with tea and coffee on tap all day. The reception staff were helpful and booked an attraction for us as well as arranging our return trip to the airport on the shuttle bus (slightly cheaper then getting a cab but just as good). This is a really great value for money hotel in a excellent location. Would stay here again and would happily recommend.

<Author>SAM2008
<Content>Great Location, Friendly Staff The hotel itself is very retro in decor so it wouldn't have been my first choice upon booking but due to it being the first week in December there wasn't a lot of vacacnies in this price range so we gave it a chance. <Author>Pumpers
<Content>Perfert City Break Hotel We stayed at this hotel for 4 nights at the beginning of Dec 2007 and for a city break this has everything you could ask for.The first impression was great because the hotel had beautiful Christmas decorations outside and a friendly concierge waiting to open the doors for you as you step out of the cab.The reception staff were very helpful friendly and knowledgeable and more than happy to answer any questions about subway stops, attractions, fares, even recommending cheap airport transport options....simply anything.The room (ours was a basic double room, not a suite) was very clean, warm and comfortable although a little small but who is going to spend time in their hotel room in NY, apart from sleeping that is?) We had a full bathroom with plenty of hot water, a mini bar (expensive as always but there if you wanted it) a safe, hairdryer and a TV.Every morning a 'continental' breakfast is served and this is complimentary. There was everything to set you up for the day bagels, toast, rolls, cereals, fresh fruit, cheese, yogurts, muffins and pastries. We only drink decaffeinated coffee and were sure we would be unlucky but sure enough it was there on tap and coffee is available in the lounge 24 hours a day, very welcome when you come back from a long day seeing the sights on a cold Dec day.The roof terrace was reported to only be open seasonally but to our delight it was open still in Dec so we assume they mean that the bar up there isn't open all year round but it was wonderful to go up there and see the Empire State building so close up. The location of this hotel is amazing. I would forget the swanky uptown, near Central Park locations and plump for this Midtown location any time. we were able to see both the Empire State and Macy's from our roof terrace (just 2 minutes walk away), the subway station was at the end of the road and Times Sq was just a 10 minute walk away. We didn't try the hotel restaurant but directly opposite the Metro is Brendan's, which is a very traditional diner/bar with high ceilings and mosaic floors, the burgers were good too. Also there were 2 Irish bar/restaurants two minutes along the roadAll in all this hotel had thought of everything you could need on a city break to the Big Apple, there was even a gym if you still had energy after pounding the sidewalks. If there was one complaint it would have to be the lifts which were slow and unable to cope with the packed hotel but they are in the process of renovating these and notices are up apologising for the inconvenience so you can't complain because they are aware and are trying to make them better.We met many people who had stayed at this hotel before and had come back to stay again and we will certainly be among them on our return to wonderful New York!!  
<Date>Jan 8, 2008

<Author>jdisney
<Content>Perfect location for a sightseing/shopping trip A very late review of our stay!We booked 5 nights at Hotel Metro through Virgin Holidays UK. The visit was part of our honeymoon, and one of the main reasons we booked this hotel was the location  roof top bar.We were very disappointed that the roof terrace was closed for renovation as we hadnt been told - Virgin however refunded us 15% of the cost for this.We booked a deluxe room, and was surprised to find this was right opposite the lifts, so we heard the lifts going up  down through the night  people coming  going.The room was quite small, but we expected this having stayed in other NYC hotels previously. It was big enough though for the 2 of us, a LOT of luggage and a small table. Bed very comfy, room very clean, bathroom overflowing with toiletries. Huge TV with a good choice of channels. Free safe inside the wardrobe.The staff were friendly and helpful in booking us airport transfers and making recommendations. We used the free internet service to email home  update them on our wedding  honeymoon which we found really useful.The major selling point of this hotel is the location - in 5 days, we only took 1 taxi (to Ground zero/statue of librety) and could walk everywhere else.15 mins Times Square, less than 5 mins to Macy's/34th street shops  Empire State building, 25mins to Central Park  main 5th Avenue shops, 15 mins to Grand Central.We did get a 48hr all loops tour on Grayline open top buses from Times Square which was brilliant - we got on  off where we wanted to, and it was great for seeing all areas of New York that we may have not took a taxi to or had time to walk to.The night tour was brilliant - especially over the Brooklyn Bridge!Another selling point of the hotel was the breakfast - it was included and there was a good selection. 24hr tea  coffee was fab as well after a long day sightseeing or shopping.I would stay in this hotel again - the small cons were far outweighed by the pros - and would recommend this to anyone -in fact, my parents are booked to stay there for their 1st trip to NYC in 3 weeks time!!If you want luxury then its not for you, but if you want a comfortable, clean place to stay in a fab location that is in a slightly higher class then yor comfort inn/travel inn, then this is the place for you. I dont think you can beat the location of this place!Make sure you take a trip to Bubba Gump Shrimp restaurant in Times Square, Top of the Rock (which we thought had better views then Empire State), a carriage ride through Central Park  trip to see the Statue of Liberty.

<Author>MyMica
<Content>Enjoyable stay at the Metro Walked from Grand Central to the Metro - found it easy to find, and the art deco bright neon sign was nice and set the tone for the hotel. Check in was quick, the room was very nicely appointed, if small (as I expected). Looked like it had recently been redone, and the linens and pillows made it feel like it was a more upscale hotel. No complaints at ALL about the room. The lobby and breakfast room were also very nice, and art deco styled -- felt very New York. And there's a very good free breakfast, and free coffee or tea anytime, day or night.The lowest point of the hotel is the staff. The doorman regularly would not even attempt to help us with the door, even when we arrived back with large Christmas gifts! The front desk staff were adequate, but one time they continued their conversation well after I'd walked up to the counter. But they recommended a great restaurant -- Brendan's -- so I give them kudos for that!

<Author>al-jh
<Content>A Great First Time In NYC At The Metro We stayed at the Metro for 3 nights at the end of November. We booked through Virgin, flew into JFK and had arranged transfers through Virgin to the hotel which took us right to the door. Check in was very effecient and didnt take long. We were allocated a room on the 7th floor opposite the lifts, which did cause us a bit of noise when the lift stopped on our floor late at night.The room was quite spacious. Bed was extremely comfy - particularly after walking round all day. Bathroom was an adequte size with an abundance of toiletries left to use. There was a large TV in a cabinet which offered a good channel choice. Plenty of storage space available for clothes etc plus ironing board and iron. Use of room safe was FREE, really good for keeping documents and money nice and safe while out and about. Use of the internet at the Metro is also FREE and can be booked at reception. No drinks making facilities in room itself but drinks machine available in dining area 24 hours a day and can take them up to rooms.Continental breakfast had a good choice on offer with cereals, fresh fruit, bagels, toast, croissants, jams and extra large size muffins ( which were gorgeous). The dining area is lovely and casual with some chairs and tables but also some armchairs and sofas for those who really like to chill out over breakfast. For those who wanted to, you can take breakfast up to your room. The best thing about the Metro is its location. Right between 5th  6th Avenues, a subway station on the corner of the street and literally a couple of minutes walk to Broadway, the Empire State and Macys. Getting around to anywhere from the Metro was easy!!A couple of recommendations - A traditional NY deli on 5th Avenue called the Green PeaAn American diner off Times Square called Brooklyns (have the cheesecake)An Irish bar off Times Square called O' Lunneys ( very friendly)A Korean bar called Red almost next to the Metro (cocktails $5 on Happy Hour)We are already talking about visiting New York again next December and will stay again at the Metro.

<Author>moescotland
<Content>Excellent location; decent hotel We chose the Metro Hotel on 35th Street street, as it was recommended by our Tavel Agent for it's excellent Manahattan location. The location is ideal - about 10 mins away from Time Square, literally round the corner from the Empire State Building and with the nearest subway only a couple of minutes away.Room were very tidy, air conditioned and are cleaned daily. The rooms include a TV and a safe. My complaint about the room is that we had a brick wall in our direct view from the window. Although the bathroom was well maintained, it is really small.The hotel has a nice 30s art-deco theme throughout. The restaurant is overpriced and it is better to eat from outside the hotel, as it is better value for money. The free daily breakfast is nice, and a good mix of cakes, breads, fruit, cereals and drinks are available. Reception staff can be approachable at times, but rude at other times, depending on how busy they are. Ideal only for it's location, but would consider trying out another hotel within the same area when i return to NYC.Approx times from hotel to:Empire State Building - few minutes walkTime Square - 10 minute walkGroundZero - 10 mins (subway)Madison Square Garden - 10 minute walkFifth Avenue - 15 minute walk

<Author>HappyTravellers21
<Content>Good Value We stayed at the Hotel Metro for 5 nights from 28th Oct. We booked with Virgin in the UK and also pre-booked all our excursions. We had 2 'Superior ' rooms on the 2nd floor, one for my husband and I, and one for our teenage daughters. Both rooms were a decent size, well furnished with comfy double beds and well equipped bathrooms. There was plenty of hot water and the shower was very powerful. The towels were changed daily and the toiletries replaced. The rooms were up only one flight of stairs so we never had to use the lifts, other than to go and check out the roof top terrace/bar which gave a very close up view of the Empire State Building.The only problem with one of the rooms was that it was on the front of the hotel and the noise from 3.00am, on the street ,was horrendous eg collection of garbage, deliveries etc. If possible request a room at the back of the hotel, the only noise our daughters heard was the hum from an outside air-con unit.The reception staff/concierge were very friendly and helpful ,always enquiring if we needed any directions etc. The breakfast was also very good with enough choice to get you well fed before venturing out. We liked the informal lounge where you sat to eat it. Coffee/Tea was available free at any time.The hotel was quite well placed for all the sights particularly the ESB and Maceys. Go to the ESB at night if you can, there's hardly any queues but remember to take some ID with you - they prefer it if you've got a photocopy of your passport. Having pre-booked all our sightseeing/excursion tickets before we travelled we were very pleased to find these waiting for us at the hotel when we arrived. I would recommend doing this if you want to do a Helicopter Flight or a trip to Niagra which we did. One word of warning though - the Niagra trip (by air) is a very long day - pick up at 6.15am arrive back at the hotel at 10.30pm. Having said that, its a great trip and very quiet at this time of year. The Maid of the Mist ride finishes on the 24th Oct so we were disappointed to miss this as the Virgin rep had said it ran until 31st Oct.We would definitely stay at this hotel again - it is slightly old fashioned, but very well run, clean, handily placed and represents good value for money.

<Author>zapokee
<Content>Very disappointing We called ahead after making our 5-night booking online to specify that we were two males and a double bed would not be appropriate, but we were allocated to a room with a queen bed that would have been tight even for a couple.  The manager told us there was nothing he could do. His reasoning was that the small print at the bottom of the reservation stated that rooms suitable for a couple or two singles were available for the booking we had made, and because we had a room suitable for a couple, the hotel had met its obligations.  It was also clear that twin rooms were available throughout our stay; we heard other people being offered the choice of a twin or a double on checking in, and saw a number of twin rooms being made up after guests had checked out. We suspect that the twin rooms were being held because they command a higher rate. The only concession we were offered was some extra blankets to enable one of us to sleep on the floor!  Other than this, the hotel was basic. The photos on the website make it look rather fancy, but while clean, the decor is quite old and rather shabby past the reception area. The spectacular-looking rooftop bar, which is presented as a major feature on the website, was closed the whole time we were there. We were informed that its opening was seasonal.  Our room was small, as was the bathroom, which had no fan or ventilation of any kind. Water leaked onto the floor through the closed shower door.  We ended up using the stairs for much of the time because the lifts were slow to the point of being unusable. Request a lower floor if you do decide to stay here.  The location of the hotel is very convenient, but there are many other conveniently located hotels in Manhattan. We would not stay here again.

<Author>The_Truffles
<Content>A very well located clean hotel I stayed at the Hotel Metro for six nights on business. Whilst I was slightly reticent at the prospect of staying in Midtown - which is hardly the nicest part of Manhatten - I was actually pleasantly surprised all 'round.Location wise, you are a very short walk indeed from either 34 Herald (N,Q,R,W trains if you're going downtown to Wall Street/Battery Park and Liberty Island and the B,D,F and V trains if you're off to Queens or the Lower East Side, both of which are worth a visit) and only another block again to Penn Station. You're two blocks from Time Square and two again to the Empire State Building and only from Macys. It's only a ten to fifteen minute walk up to the top of Fifth Avenue if you want to take in the sights as well.But, the best part is that despite being in such a great location, you're not slap bang in the middle of the tourist horror traps of Time Square. You don't step out of the hotel into the latest wave of back-packing students, or hoardes of tour groups that insist on standing the full width of the pavement.The hotel itself is modest, but was spotless, as was my room. I have stayed in more expensive hotels that have not provided a room as immaculate as the one I stayed in.One tip, though - if you can, ask for a room at the back of the hotel. The rooms on the front can be noisy on account of passing traffic (it's not a busy road, but New Yorkers tend to use their horns at every possible opportunity). It didn't help that next door but one to the hotel is a construction site that was operating 24 hours a day. The bed was very comfortable, the pillows a generous size and the housekeeping staff attentive and civil. Whilst the hotel may be looking a little dated, it's not horrific and was very clean throughout.The fitness studio was very good indeed. Sorry to labour the point, but there are more expensive hotels out there that provide nothing more than a few mismatching dumbells and a third-hand treadmill. The fitness equipment was very new, offered a good range of choice and the area was air-conditioned and served by two huge flat screens. On the roof of the hotel is a very unusual and pleasant terrace which offers some nice views and must be very nice in the summer months.My room had a new iron and ironing board in the room, a decent safe, decent size TV and a speaker system that will fit your iPod, so you can even take your favourite tunes with you.If you want a magnificant, opulent hotel that will rip you off on the room rate and cost of breakfast - rather then the very ample and free breakfast consisting of a big range of different bagels, breads, fresh juice, coffee, breakfast cereals, yoghurts etc served at the Metro - then this isn't for you.Considering the price, the great location and standards of the rooms, it's certainly worth giving serious thought to staying here. I was a satisfied guest of the Metro and would stay there again. This hotel is particuarly suitable for tourists who want the convenience of being Midtown but who don't want to be right on top of Times Square and the associated noise and problems that brings. In addition, if you're on business, you're very well placed to take a short walk uptown or hop on the Metro to go to Wall Street.  
<Date>Nov 10, 2007

<Author>erster
<Content>Unhappy Metro Guest This was my second time at the Metro; I booked a room there because my first impressions had been so positive. This time, however, I had a number of problems and even though the location is great, probably won't go back. The only rooms available were directly opposite the elevators, which emit a very loud DING DONG every time they stop at a floor -- not conducive to peaceful repose. There was only one really functional elevator (a sign posted announced that they were doing an elevator revitalization project) and therefore it took a long time to get up and down -- the service elevator was also usable, but took equally long and frequently--no surprise-- was full of cleaning carts and plumbers. The mini bar was empty -- except for one can of coke -- and on inquiring I was told that they were refurbishing the mini-bars, upgrading them, but hadn't gotten around to all the rooms yet! The business center is a joke -- you have to check out a special key card at the front desk, with a time limit of a half hour. I discovered this one morning when I'd spent several minutes of futility inserting my own key card. Having just stocked up on coffee and a muffin in the breakfast room, I went down one flight to the lobby to ask why my room key didn't work -- and was informed by the desk clerk that no food or drinks were allowed in the business center, and that before he let me sign the key out, I had to leave the coffee/muffin in my room. Since I didn't want to spend another five or more minutes trying to get the elevator up to and back from the ninth floor, I said that I'd just leave the grub outside the business center room while I checked my email. He reiterated that it was hotel policy not to take food in there. I said I wasn't challenging that and would leave it on the table outside the room. He kept hassling me about it until finally I invited him to follow me up there so that he, personally, could verify that I wasn't taking any forbidden substances in with me! At that point, he said, suit yourself, and with a great show of reluctance let me have the key. I don't think I've ever encountered such offensive and disrespectful behavior in any hotel, in NYC or elsewhere. To be fair, there were some very pleasant people on the staff as well, and the room itslef was comfortable, spacious, and clean. But I can't imagine anything that might induce me to stay there next time I'm in New York -- or ever again! Even if they stock the mini bars!  
<Date>Nov 5, 2007

<Author>SanMateoMee
<Content>Great deal for NYC, and perfect for families We booked the suite that includes one large room with two queen beds, another bedroom with one queen bed, and one bathroom. I was in NYC with my parents, so this was a perfect and economical set up for us ($450/night for the suite). The hotel is clean, the staff friendly, it's located a half block from a major subway line and a half block from 5th Avenue, and it includes a perfectly adequate breakfast buffet to get you going in the morning (yogurt, fruit, cereal, muffins, bagels, etc). The Metro Grill (attached to the restaurant) was much better than I expected it to be and was quite reasonably priced. There are several Korean restaurants on the block. We ate at the one two doors down from the hotel twice, and it was very good. The hotel isn't fancy, but it is clean and the rooms are well appointed. I highly recommend it, especially for price compared to other hotels in NYC.
