<Author>JaneBradshaw
<Content>A geat free breakfast! After much teeth gnashing having read so many poor reviews of NY hotels, we finally settled on the Metro. The location is okay, very near Macy's and with enough bars and eating places to choose from after along day's sight seeing. I booked a double room which is what we got. There was one bed and the room was very compact. It had a decent shower cubicle within the very small bathroom and also had iron and ironing board, free safe etc. I would recommend that you book a twin room as you will get 2 double beds and a much much bigger room. The hotel has a very pricy roof bar, but a great view of the Empire State building. Worth a visit if only on the first night. There is a gym too on the top floor.The hotel provides free hot drinks all day and a great free breakfast: juice, hot drinks, fruit, cereal , yoghurt etc as well as all the baked goods you would expect in the US. Breakfast is available until 11am. Overall, this is a good hotel, clean, safe and close to subways. Times Square is a 10 min walk away.

<Content>Great location My Mom and I just returned from a three night stay here and we loved it! Had a queen size bed - room not huge but definitely ample for two people. You aren't going to be in there much anyway! Great location - we felt safe walking around at night. Helpful staff - they gave excellent directions to every attraction we wanted to visit. The included breakfast is a great bonus - bagels, muffins, yogurt, granola, etc. This saved us some money and was a nice way to start the day. You can be at Macy's within 5 minutes and in Times Square in just over 10 minutes. We were nervous about the subway at first but when we return we will ride it from day one. Metro staff told us how many stops to expect and where to go when the train stops. The view of the Empire State Building from the rooftop terrace is awe inspiring. I suggest walking up in the daytime and at night when it is lit up for some beautiful photos. The only complaint we had was that the elevators were painfully slow but they were working on them so that should be improved soon.

<Content>Will Return Again We stayed at Hotel Metro for the very first time a couple of days before Christmas in 2006. The room that we stayed is smaller, and the view from our room faced the alley. The hotel is in a great location, but it's quiet at night. We definitely will return again!

<Author>WI-Couple
<Content>Average hotel for a good price Being that hotel prices in Manhattan are ridiculously high, I searched high and low to find a reasonably priced hotel. The Hotel Metro fit the bill in that it: was in a good location, had good ratings, had a reasonable (for NYC) price.The pros:* Excellent location within walking distance of Time Square and the Theatre District* WONDERFUL continental breakfast! Lots of variety, clean/organized presentation and lots of places to sit with friends or alone watching CNN on large screen TVs.* FREE WiFi in the rooms* The staff was helpful and efficientThe cons:* SOOOO Noisy! I was on the 9th floor, had brought ear plugs and turned on the air conditioner and TV to drown out the street noise and it still hardly worked one night. There must be a garbage collection right below here as I could hear the dumpsters getting thrown around for hours?!?* The rooms and especially the bathrooms are small (I understand its NYC, I'm just warning people - compared to the two other hotels I've stayed in here, they're small).* No bathtub, just corner shower (not a problem for me, but again, informational)* Garbage left under the bed the first night, a note to the maid (along with my regular tip) cleared that up quickly.* Slightly musty smell in the bathroom, but I may be especially sensitive as I've noticed it in many of the more historic hotels.Overall I rate this as average, sorry to everyone who loved it, but I just didn't think it was all that special. If its the right price, I'd certainly recommend it as there's nothing seriously wrong with the hotel, but I just can't rave about it as others have.

<Author>Bucky_Sinclair
<Content>Pleasant Stay From Start to Finish I'd like you to consider disregarding many of the reviews of Hotel Metro that seemed to nit-pick. YES, the elevators are small and slow, and yes, there's construction next door that ties things up a bit and makes for some early weekday clatter. Otherwise, I really liked this hotel and can recommend it completely. Pleasant front-desk help, great location near the 34th St. subway station, delightful complementary continental breakfast, clean, well-appointed rooms, and a cool rooftop patio with an incredible view of the Empire State Building. It's not a resort or a five-star hotel. But for the money I don't think you'll be at all disappointed at the Hotel Metro. As a disclaimer, I should add that through some unique alignment of the planets, or a stroke of good karma for your correspondent, my reservation through hotels.com for a basic room was upgraded to a penthouse room at no charge. I don't exactly live on a farm, but staying in the lap of (increased) luxury tends to influence one's perceptions of experiences. I hope you strike similar good fortune when staying at Hotel Metro in NYC.

<Author>QueenBeeLondon
<Content>Fantastic stay at the Metro I took my boyfriend away for his birthday and as it was his first visit to NYC I wanted everything to be perfect. He is also quite hard to please when it comes to hotels and as I had been to NYC before I knew how hard it was going to be to find decent accommodation for a reasonable price. As always I scoured trip advisor and found the Hotel Metro was ticking many of my boxes. What we found when we arrived at the hotel exceeded every expectation and more. The location is absolutely perfect. It is right in the middle of all of the hustle and bustle of Manhattan but 35th street itself (street of the hotel) is a little oasis of calm in between all the madness. The staff were so friendly and helpful and couldn't do enough to help me organise surprise birthday treats. The room was really clean (lovely toiletries) and every day we came back to a made bed and fresh towels. Also, if you want to counteract all the food you end up eating then there is a fantastic air conditioned gym on the penthouse floor complete with big screen tv. This in turn leads out onto a lovely roof terrace. It's a nice place to chill in the morning and a busy little place to have drinks in the evening. One of the great sellers for the hotel is the complimentary breakfast. This is hard to find in NYC but was a perfect way to start the day. There was a great choice of fresh fruit, bagels, toast, muffins etc and we would have been lost with out it.I really can't recommend this Hotel enough. It is a real lottery to find decent places to stay and still not spend ridiculous money for the privilege. With the Hotel Metro you will have definitely won the jackpot. If it can more than satisfy a fussy couple like us then it must be doing something right.

<Author>Polly35
<Content>Great location and breakfast I stayed at Hotel Metro in mid August 2007, with my sister. On arrival we had we requested a twin room via booking through a website and I was very disappointed to find that we did not have a twin room.We were told that because we had booked through a website, a twin room could not be guaranteed unless booking direct with the hotel. Not a good start to a 5 night trip!! Especially as iIhad rung the night before to ensure we had a twin room. However by the next day, one of the hotel staff , George, came to the rescue and was able to move us to a twin room. He was polite, helpful, friendly and charming and really improved our stay at the Hotel Metro. If you want a twin room or anything else for that matter, ring the hotel directy and speak to George if posssible. The hotel was also in a great location, 200 yards from the metro (buy a 7 day metro card- really economical if you are using the subway a lot) and round the corner from Macys and 5th Ave. Also the complimentay breakfasts (muffins, toast, pastries, cereal etc) from 6-11am was a real added bonus, along with coffee available all day. The rooms were a great size (for New York) though bathrooms a little small but functional. We had a great 6 days, shopping (Century 21-great! 11% discount card available for visitors at Macys and Bloomies) and eating ( Book restaurants beforehand, especially weekends) !! The hotel can arrange a transfer to a NY airport when you leave the busy city for home!!

<Author>vamp555
<Content>Great location, a real gem I just wanted to add a review for Hotel Metro to endorse most of the comments added.We stayed in November 2006 for 6 nights on our first trip to New York. The hotel is in a fantastic location with Macy's and the Empire State building very near by.The room was very clean and maid service excellent. The room was average sized with the bed very comfortable and a great shower. There were fresh towels daily and the bed was also changed every day.We found the staff very helpful and always friendly. Our in room safe was not working and within 15 minutes of reporting to reception a maintenence guy knocked on our door and fixed it. The reception staff were always willing to help with queries and booked us some tours and the airport taxi service with no problems.The 24 hour coffee in the lobby was always appreciated. We needed to ask for fresh milk a couple of times but this was sorted with a smile! The breakfast was plentiful every morning consisting of bagels, muffins and fresh fruit.The rooftop terrace looks out onto the Empire State building and is a lovely place to sit in the evening after being on your feet all day. Being November it was never busy but I bet in summer it gets crowded.We would recommend this hotel to any traveller. We will certainly be booking to stay here again.

<Author>elestoban
<Content>thanks to other reviewers Firstly thanks to all reviewers of the Metro  other NYC hotels - we studied them carefully but decided the Metro was the most likely to suit us best  I think it did.Room size is a lottery, ours 1215, was small by any standard ( except maybe cheaper hotels in Paris ) however 1214 was large as was 1209 opposite the lifts.The bathroom was minute but well planned  the shower was good. Towels  toiletries good. The air con was a little noisy. The room was very well appointed with top quality furnishings,spotlesslyy clean  a very comfortable bed. The mini bar was hopeless beverages would have been cooler out of it. I asked for it to be fixed  George displayed great empathy but it remained useless for the whole of our stay. There is a lot of building work adjacent to the hotel  therefore it may be noisy at the front. We had requested a high up room  were offered a choice of front or back by charming receptionist.Breakfast is cereals,fruit,yogurt,muffins  bagels - all self service  disposable cutlery,plates,bowls etc. Very good  no signs encouraging tips.Staff friendly. Terrace bar a bit of a dissapointment - plastic glasses  tacky signs saying table service only The location as widely reported is fantastic 34th str subway station is 100yds from hotel - yes on 35th Str.All day fun pass on subway  buses $7 - less than the minimum fare on the London tube!! Cleaner than the tube as well. Ignore any reports of it being in a poor,rough or run down neighbourhood. Its just spoilt a little by the building work  scaffolding nearby however there is building work  scaffolding ALL over New York incl 5th Ave  The Waldorf Astoria.it cost $280 a night which is more than we would have liked but compared to all the others that we researched it seemed to be good value certainly helped by free tea  coffee  a good breakfast served from 6.30 until 11.00am . Whilst Hotel was slightly more than would have been ideal everything else seemed either cheap or good value - of couse almost 2 to the pound helped.! We were there during a heatwave  that may have been partly to blame for poor air con in corridors  especially the lift. We enjoyed our stay , didnt mind our small room  feel that we wouldnt have done any better for the price.Whilst in NYC consider an off Broadway show Tony  Tina's wedding - do yr own research it wont appeal to all. we loved it.

<Author>Antonia_7
<Content>Some positives, mostly neutral, great location Please have patience whilst I get something off my chest - why are some of the other reviewers basing tsome of their criticism on some neighbourhood properties  some of the hotel guests being of Far East origin??? I think that closed-minded travellers who wish to visit somewhere that does not contain a 'melting pot' of cultures are rather naive in choosing to visit New York. Afterall, isn't the wonderful preponderance of Minority Ethnic neighbourhoods, cultures  cuisines one of the truly great things about New York?? Plus, the restaurants referred to ignorantly as 'Chinese' are actually Korean. And the rubbish that was left outside them was the same rubbish left outside every NY restaurant every night!!! OK, the hotel - not brilliant, but not bad either. Luckily we did not come across any evidence of mice at all, and may feel defirrently if we had. The hotel seems expensive compared to other US destinations, but is a pretty standard price for London for example, and you expect higher prices for NY. Our room was very small (but again we expected that) but very clean. We enjoyed the MP3 docking station/speaker unit, the breakfast was useful (toast, bagels, fruit, yoghurts, chesse, ham, cereal, danish pastries, muffins, TC  juice), and the 24/7 TC was very very useful. The staff were neither friendly nor rude, they got the job done in a quiet non-chatty way - so nothing to rave about, but crucially no complaints either. The lifts were limited  slow, so we often took the stairs, but again - you only have to wait 2 or 3 minutes  it would arrive. We didn't have any problems with noise  we thought the location was superb - v close to subway stop/Macys/Empire State Building. THe area felt very safe, we often returned at 22.00 to 01.00 and didn't feel worried about doing so- the 24 hour Korean restaurants next door help this as there is always a pretty lively crowd outside. There is a newsagents to the left of the hotel for drinks  papers, the area is slightly whiffy - but it only takes you 1 minute to walk through it  then you're back in the excitement of New York. This hotel is a perfectly decent place from which to see NY, it is better than 'basic' but not luxurious, the rooftop bar is still closed. If you just want somewhere to bed for the night, get a decent shower, good air con, have a cup of tea after hitting the city  a free breakfast to get you ready for the day - this is it. Just don't expect huge rooms, smiley 'have a nice day' service  low prices. (Extras - if you're buying an iPod in NY make sure it is actually the gB requirement you need - don't accept the sellers reassurances that 'this is 8gB' for example - especially around Times Sqaure. Bargain hard, walk away  the price gets knocked down by $$$- over $150 off the asking price for a Sony camera for us. Half price ticket booths for Theatre tix are well worth it despite the wait of up to 2hrs - great seats, especially for Weds matinees - for $55. Chicago  The Colour Purple were both superb - the first very polished, the latter very moving. Washington Square is wonderful for people watching, and dog watching, at the weekend. The New York Water Taxi is a great way to take a trip over to Brooklyn, ~$11 pp with excellent views of the Statue of Liberty)  
<Date>Jul 13, 2007

<Author>lemonadepocket
<Content>Great location and free coffee! Friends recommended us to this hotel and we are so pleased they did. Friendly staff, clean rooms and a great location near the Empire State, Macy's, Time Sq and the Rockefeller Centre. The area immediately around the hotel wasn't great - lots of construction work so noise and dust but we always felt safe. The roof terrace was still closed for refurb although we saw little sign of any work going on. Our room overlooked the multi-storey car park so no view but clean and comfortable and the shower was wonderful! One small criticism is their strict rules over the mini-bar and fridge. We didn't put it to the test, but the info says that if you even lift something up to look at it for more than 20 seconds, it will be charged to your room! Our supplies weren't filled until the third or fourth day we were there and so we hadn't realised there should have been more chocolate and stuff. They tried to charge us but we refused and they were okay about it. You couldn't use the fridge to store any of your own drinks (even water) at all.The breakfast room got pretty full but it was a great not to have to go out to find breakfast. If anyone keeps kosher, there are two or three restaurants and a deli within a couple of blocks.

<Author>miercoles
<Content>Not as good as everybody says... I, like many of you, before deciding which hotel to choose, tend to spend hours and hours on places like this finding the best hotel for the money. I read a lot of excellent reviews of this hotel and on the outside sources the hotel's website mention. So, even tough this hotel was a little more expensive than the others I was planning to choose, I decided to book this hotel based solely on the reviews I read. The hotel is not bad but it's not the wonder people tend to believe. It is located in a block surrounded by chinese/korean commerce (of course, not the kind of place like Chinatown) but just regular bars and hotels but with a an almost 99% asian clientele. The room size is good from a NYC point of view, but the bathrooms are tiny. The very first day I used the bathroom, one of the towels tray went off and it stayed there my whole stay. I didn't care for asking in the desk for its repair but the cleaning personal saw that tray broken every day and they didn't have the iniative to ask for its repair. The hotel staff is neutral, nor friendly, nor rude, except one day when the staff at the desk was rude and uninterested. The hotel is clean and the bed is confortable, the complimentary breakfast is a plus. But let me tell you that I didn't find this hotel nothing extraordinary nor charming and I doubt I'll be back again because I know there are equal or even better hotels with better prices than this one. Hotel Metro is not as good as they want you to believe.

<Author>DC_World_Traveler
<Content>Quirky with Great Geography If location's all you're after, this may be the hotel for you! The Hotel Metro is a half block from the subway and Harald Square/Macy's, and only a five minute walk from Penn Station and Madison Square Garden. It has nice thick cotton towels and free internet access during specified hours in a key-carded room for which you must procure a pass from the front desk. That's where the good points end. My major gripe was that there was a strange rustling sound, that may have been a rodent in the wall, which woke me up all night in my room. At first I thought it was air conditioner condensate dripping, or the mini bar sensor, so I turned off the A/C and later unplugged the frig. The sound persisted and kept me from sleeping much for the two nights I spent there. There was no noise during the day. It was kind of creepy and unsettling. Room 710 was average size, about 16x12 with cutouts and a small bathroom with almost no counterspace and a bathtowel-sized floorspace. I was told I was being upgraded to a king, and I thought it was all talk, until I saw the tiny rooms with almost no walking space when the maids left doors open along the hallways. Furnishings and carpet were dingy gold, brown, orange, and the fake marbled bathroom had incongruous plastic cups and thick, comfy white cotton towels. The rooftop which everyone raves about was closed, there was heavy construction going on immediately to the west of the building, and that block of W. 35th is seedy and filthy. Location is ok, but it's overpriced for the amenities and questionable rodent problem. I only stayed there because I couldn't find a room at any 4 stars+ in the city that weekend due to multiple events.  
<Date>Jun 6, 2007

<Author>ValGardener
<Content>Great location, great breakfast My husband and I stayed at the Hotel Metro in late April, 2007. We loved it. We were initially put in a smoking room, but our request to change to a non-smoking room was immediately granted. The new room was very small but at least it didn't smell like smoke.The room we were in seemed to be recently renovated, the carpet was new and fluffy. The bathroom was marble. The shower was great - high pressure and no waiting for hot water.There is free high-speed wireless, and a safe. While we were there, our clock radio was switched out to one with mp3 hookup - nice touch! Too bad I didn't bring my ipod.The best part was the location - near Macy's and the Empire State building. Very central regardless of where you want to spend your time in Manhattan. A subway stop is a few steps away.The continental breakfast was free, fresh, and good.Overall, I'd recommend this hotel, especially for the price.

<Author>Clarts
<Content>I would be happy to stay there again We stayed at the Metro for 4 nights at the end of March in a superior room. We asked for non smoking but on arrival we were told the rooms were smoking, but were brand new and would not smell. They did. To be fair to the check in staff we were told in advance we could change but after a very long day we could not be bothered and decided we would leave the windows open. I regretted this after the first flush of the toilet which wouldn`t stop filling up and flooded the bathroom. Fortunately I found the stop valve and prevented it flooding the bedroom. One call to reception and staff were quickly on scene. No further problems. Whilst on the subject of the bathroom, it was TINY, the smallest I have encountered in any hotel. Anyone sat on the loo would be instantly kneecapped by another person opening the door.As previously mentioned in other postings the breakfast is a nice touch. The chocolate muffins are excellent but you need to grab them as soon as you go in otherwise someone else will. The breakfast room itself is not very big but has an informal atmosphere. The all day coffee/ tea was also very welcome.The hotel is in a good location for most things. I agree with previous posters about Heartlands brewery just around the corner, good choice of beer and food. Also worth a visit is the place directly across the road from the Hotel Metro, Brendans I think it was called. Reasonably priced and not too far too walk back ! No complaints about the staff, ther were friendly and informative but one observation. I asked for a quote for a taxi back to Newark airport and was told 90 dollars including tip. I had used Carmel from the incoming flight which was 60 dollars including tip.Reception staff had not heard of Carmel and suggested if I booked a company from the phone book they might not turn up ? I`m sure there are better hotels in New York but the Metro ticks most of the boxes and I would be happy to go there again.

<Author>Bulldog1037
<Content>Worth every penny!! We stayed here because we were going to a late night birthday party. I had read many of the previous reviews and was still pleasantly surprised by this hotel. The front desk was well staffed and helpful. Complimentary coffee and tea are offered throughout the day. We arrived around 4pm and decided to go shopping. Talk about a perfect location! Herald Square is less than a block away. Our room was small, but very clean and pleasant with a view of the rooftops out back. The minibar is charged based on the weight of items. Do not remove anything unless you expect to be charged for that item. Aside from the basic cleanliness and convenience of this location, we were surprised at the quality of the food in the Metro Grill. My husband and I had a wonderful dinner! The atmosphere leaves something to be desired, but the Ravioli Aurora and the Salmon were both excellent!Lots of value in this location!

<Author>Irishgirl1212
<Content>Nice stay 13-21 March First thing first the staff were very friendly especially one of the doormen who recommended the show Curtains (an older gentleman and unfortunately I can't recall his name). The show was brillinat by the way. On our first night we were allocated a room on the top floor but were woken at 8am the next morning by the builders working on the terrace. Once we informed the reception staff we were moved to another room. Might want to question whether the works are completed on the terrace before accepting a room on the 12th floor. The whole hotel including our room was spotless. Another bonus when staying at the Metro is the free breakfast. Bagels, toast, muffins, fruit, juice, tea, coffee and so forth were all yummy and more than enough to do you for the day. You could also take breakfast up to the room if you fancy breakfast in bed (breakfast staff will happily organise a tray for you). It might be a bit repetitive to have breakfast in the hotel each day but it can save you a fortune.Great location as many people have described. Nearest metro stop is 100 yards away 34th St/Herald Square. I would recommend Brendans bar across the street from the hotel. Nice bar with a great atmosphere (hotel bar was nice but usually empty). Free wifi in the room - absolutely brilliant especially those like me who can't live without their laptop. The hotel room also has a laptop sized safe which even my wide screen laptop could fit into. Overall it was a nice hotel and I would stay here again. I have recommended this hotel to family and friends too.

<Author>cotagirl
<Content>Nice hotel....good breakfast! After reviewing many hotels on this site, I ended up choosing the Metro for a 4 night trip to NYC with my mom and cousin. I mainly chose this for the location and for the fact that a breakfast was included. It was very nice to have the continental breakfast as an option in the mornings, and saved us from having to buy breakfast or coffee elsewhere. The 24 hr. coffee/tea service in the lobby was a nice touch as well.The location of the hotel was awesome. It was a quick walk to the next block for both Macy's and the Empire State Bldg. We usually took a cab everywhere else because the weather was so cold while we were there. A cab ride to Times Square was about 6 dollars and approx. 5-10 minutes depending on traffic. Also about the same $ and time for a cab to any of the theatres.Overall, the hotel was a good value by NYC standards. Our room happened to be a wheelchair-accessible room, so it was obviously larger than what the normal room size would be. Therefore, the three of us had plenty of space in a room with two double beds. I can't comment on the space issue in the average room. We were located (I think) on the back of the hotel, and there was no view at all from our window. But it didn't matter because we truly weren't in the room long enough anyway. Who wants to hang out in their hotel while in NYC??We did have a couple of minor problems with our room though that I should comment on. Our toilet continued to malfunction and we had to have maintenance there several times. Also the battery on our door lock started to go dead in the middle of the night (which resulted in a constant low beeping noise from 2 AM until we left the room at 9 AM). Apparently the front desk person was unable to change the battery and maintenance had to be contacted for this problem. This was a bit irritating to us, and the front desk wasn't very accomodating. Overall, the staff wasn't very helpful and/or friendly (with the exception of one bellman--an older gentleman and unfortunately I can't recall his name).So in summary, I would recommend this hotel for price, location, breakfast/coffee---but hopefully you won't have problems that require assistance from the front desk staff. Have fun in the city!!!

<Author>GillLondon
<Content>Really pleased with chose the Metro I stayed at the Metro in New York last October and I afraid it taken me all this time to do this review. However, I did particularly want to do this review as my husband and I were so pleased that we chose the Metro. We didn know where to stay but our friends from Washington recommended the Metro. We were particularly pleased with it location, being very central, surrounded by lots of shops, within a few yards of the metro station and within walking distance of Penn Railway Station, which we needed as we were travelling onwards to Washington. The one down point was the lack of medium range restaurants in locality. We arrived in the evening and wanted to have a meal but all the restaurants nearby were fast food, serving mainly pizzas, hamburgers, hot dogs etc. We couldn find a decent reasonably priced restaurant in the area at all. Maybe someone else will be able to recommend one but we walked around for at least an hour and could find nothing. We ended up eating at the Metro Hotel restaurant which was good but it would have been nice to have a choice. We did find in most areas of the City that there were plenty of cheap fast food restaurants and also very expensive restaurants but a lack of medium range restaurants. I sure they are there tucked away in side streets but we walked a lot and didn see many. We stayed in a basic room with no upgrade and were really pleased with it. It was a little on the small size but what you would expect for the price we were paying in a major city. Everything was very clean, the bed was comfortable and the bathroom had a bath as well as a shower. The free Broadband was good and really fast. It saved us a lot on phone calls as we could E Mail our friends in Washington when to expect us etc. However, the biggest bonus was the breakfast. Our room price included Continental breakfast and we were expecting just tea/coffee and pastries but there was a really good selection, including large selection of bread/bagels, cereals, boiled eggs, cheeses, yogurts, muffins, selection of teas, coffee, hot chocolate. I have probably left things out as it hard to remember everything. There may have been cold meats but I wouldn have noticed, being a vegetarian. My only complaint would be that it was served with the usual plastic cutlery and paper plates that we found in many establishments in New York, however, I probably just being fussy, being used to standards in the UK. As it was winter we could not use the rooftop bar but I sure that would be really nice in the summer. So all in all, I would thoroughly recommend the Metro for a short city break in a central location.  
<Date>Feb 12, 2007

<Author>alisonWigan
<Content>Great hotel. Just returned from a 6 night stay at the Metro and was very impressed with it. The location is excellent being very central and close to Maceys, the Empire State Building and a subway station. I loved the art deco styling in reception and in the rooms. Our room was big enough, it had a large TV and a good bathroom with Gilchrist and Soames toiletries. I asked for a high floor and was put in a room on the 6th floor - it was at the back of the hotel so no view but no traffic noise either.We had a few problems with the safe which refused to open but once the maintenance man realised it was actually faulty and the problem didn't lie with our inability to work it, he quickly fitted a new door to it.Minor gripes were lack of coathangers and lack of shelf space in the bathroom.The free breakfast was fine I thought although my husband was disappointed there was no option for a cooked breakfast. I didn't like the disposable cutlery and crockery though - that's not helping the global warming situation!Once we checked out, the doorman was happy to store our cases and book us a taxi to the airport.Finally I must recommend Brendan's Bar and Grill across the street for excellent food at reasonable prices in a lovely setting which you would not expect from the outside.

<Author>CaroRigg
<Content>Great Hotel We just got back to the UK from an excellent 5 night stay at the Hotel Metro, W35th St, NY, arranged through Virgin Atlantic Holidays. The hotel was in a really good position half a block from Herald Square and Macy's. It was very clean and comfortable and the staff - including the room maids - were helpful, friendly and polite. Our room was large, the double bed comfortable, the good sized bathroom clean with a good shower, and the large TV (with satellite) actually worked (unlike some in other NY hotels we've stayed at previously!). There was also a mini-bar (though we didn't use it) and the heating wasn't opressive (and we could open the window). The only down side was the street noise at night (especially with the window open!) which sounded as if there was construction/rubbish collection going on all night every night - but we had been given a choice of room and chose front which probably wasn't too smart!There was free coffee available all day in the lounge (which you could take up to your room if you wanted) and a really great free breakfast - coffee, juice, fresh fruit, muffins, bagels, toast, pastries, yoghurts, cereals - you name it, everything you could possibly want short of a full cooked menu! Altogether a really great little hotel in an excellent, mid-town position, close to all the sights and convenient if you want to shop til you drop! We can thoroughly recommend it - the only thing making it fall short of an Excellent rating was the street noise at night but apart from that we couldn't fault it and would certainly stay there again.(Oh, and the Virgin flights were great too!)

<Author>runpkc
<Content>Good room. Excellent breakfast. Awesome location. Love NYC! ***My wife and I stayed at the Hotel Metro for 13 nights over Thanksgiving into the start of the Christmas rush. What a fabulous time to be in New York City (NYC), a must do!!! Lots of lights and beautiful Christmas displays everywhere, this is an opportunity for kids to really enjoy the season and adults to relive their childhood!***To the room, it was a good size with adaquate storage. The room had a laptop safe with room for other valuables as well. The washroom was a bit small but nothing we couldn't work with. ***Room service was quick when we asked for extras. We never ordered food or ate in the hotel restaurant as there are alot of dining choices around the hotel including lil Korea which is just two blocks over. We even got a few work outs in the hotel gym.*** To avoid the noise from the street, we requested a room on a higher floor near the back of the hotel. In saying this, we would use our earplugs again as noisy car horns and garbage trucks rumbling through are just part of the ambiance in NYC. *** We started each morning with a healthy serving of tasty and healthy breakfast delights in the lounge which was included in the room charge. The staff were prepared with enough food and seating to fit everyone even during days when there were big events such as Black Friday and the Macy's Day Parade. ***The hotel is centrally located to local attractions and there is a subway station 1/2 a block away. Macy's is 1/2 block away, the Empire State Building is 1 block away and Time Square is only a 10 minute walk while the uptown attractions like Central Park, Trump Tower etc are about a 25 minute walk away. ***We will book again at the Hotel Metro. Thank you to all of those who had taken the time to share their experiences on Tripadvisor.***NYC is a must see destination and very friendly city, but be prepared to open up your wallet from the time you get off the plane until you are back on the plane. It is worth everyone penny!***Thanks Tripadvisor.

<Author>suladybug
<Content>Hit and Miss I was staying at the Hotel Metro for business, so a good night's sleep was key. Unfortunately, I stayed there during an unusually warm weekend in December. They had shut the air conditioning off for the season, and all I could get out of the unit in my room was hot air--not even air from the outside. I'd estimate the temperature in my room reached about 90 degrees by bedtime. After several desperate phone calls to the front desk between midnight and 1am, someome finally came up and opened my bedroom window. But, I STILL wasn't able to sleep because of all of the street noise. The manager was very helpful the next day, and they did manage to find a room for me at the back of the hotel, where the fan did actually blow air from the outside. But, the first night was miserable. The rooms were average for New York, small and a little bit shabby. The breakfast was wonderful, though they could use more seating, and the location was terrific for my purposes. But, I would not stay again.

<Author>virgil_hilts
<Content>Nice Hotel, Fantastic Location My wife and I stayed here the weekend before Christmas, The Most Wonderful Time of the Year, which means it's the most crowded. While in a busy part of town - just a block from Macy's - the quiet seclusion of the Hotel Metro made a nice escape from our otherwise touristy weekend. We flew into JFK, took the Airtrain to Jamaica Station and the Long Island Railroad to Penn Station. This was the most economical means I could find to travel into the city ($10 per person at the non-peak time). We walked from Penn Station - which was no problem. Taking cab here could be a problem as things always seemed kind of jammed around the nearby intersections. There is also a subway stop at the 6th Ave end of the block but we actually never used it. The desk had our check-in information almost instantaneously after we arrived, even though the desk attendant was simultaneously assisting another guest with some show reservations.The room was adequately sized and very clean. It was apparent that they had gutted and older hotel at some point recently as everything had a kind of new clean feel to it. The bathroom had some nice products. No view to speak of - but we hadn't come here to stay in the room. It was very quiet in the mornings - we were on the side away from the street. The free breakfast is filling and a good starter. The free wireless internet is a great help! The rooftop terrace was closed for renovations - but I'm sure it's awesome as the Empire State Building Towers over the whole area.It's only one subway stop to Times Square, so we walked there as well - about 15 minutes - up Broadway. Saw a show at the Marquis Theater (The Drowsy Chaperone) - the ticket gave you a free pass to The View Lounge, which is usually $7. You'll need that to spring for the $15 cocktails. But it's a rotating restaurant / lounge ringed at the window by tables for 2 - so a great place for a date. We walked up 5th Avenue to Rockefeller Center and did The Top of the Rock - this was a much better experience than the Empire State Building, which I did a year ago. I was kind of shocked by the disparity between the massive crowd around the ice rink and tree and how empty / spacious it was at the top. I guess this secret isn't out yet!For all of our activities, the Hotel Metro provided and excellent base as we wanted to check out things from Central Park to Canal Street's shady shopping. It was a little pricey - but so was everything for this time of year. Overall, we had a great stay and I would stay here again.  
<Date>Dec 27, 2006

<Author>RoseD
<Content>Great location! We had transport booked from the airport to the hotel which was a good start. On arriving at the hotel the desk staff were helpful. The room was a good size and the bathroom was good too, plus plenty of nice toiletries provided everyday. The hotel was in the best location, one street from the Empire State Building and the hotel had a roof terrace which in the evening had the most amazing view of the ESB all lit up. We walked absolutely everywhere, we did not use any public transport and whilst our feet were in agony it was soo worth it as you didn't miss anything when we went places. Plus as it was in the middle of everything you could walk either right down to battery park or up to central park etc.. Was also close enough to Times Square for the evening. The breakfast was probably the only part which wasn't brilliant but it was ok, there were huge muffins and danish pastries, though if you came back in about 11 am you could have round two if you liked! or at least another coffee or fruit juice. The metro restaurant which was adjoined was really lovely and the food here was fab, we ended up eating here every night as it was so good. We booked a trip with the hotel to go on an evening boat trip around Manhattan and I would say this was the best part of the holiday, seeing lit up Manhattan at night going under Brooklyn Bridge etc it was amazing and we were lucky enough to also see a firework display on that trip which was fantastic.As to New York, get to the ESB at about 8am on a week day and you won't have to queue at all and it's worth doing the option with the speaker so you get stories as you go around the top. The views were brilliant. We went to Liberty Island in the afternoon, it was good though she's not as big as I imagined! You will have to queue to get on the boat, we didn't get off at Ellis Island but if you want to, go early as you will be queuing a long time to get back on the boat from here as it picks up the Liberty Island Trippers first and then the people from Ellis just fit in any space that is left. If you want to go up the pedestal of Liberty you have to phone to pre book or there are a limited amount of tickets on the day, though I don't think we missed much by not going inside it. Grand Central Terminal is worth a trip, even if it's just to grab something to eat, the food court downstairs is massive as are the huge sandwiches!If you want tickets from the cheap TKTS booth for Broadway shows, we went to the less crowded one down the bottom end of the island, however there wasn't much left by the time we got there so I'd recommend getting there when it opens.We were not planning on passing ground zero, however it is difficult to miss but actually does make you think and you may wish to stop by to pay respect.Also I think next time we will arrange to have one of those trips with a real New Yorker, but you have to book well in advance.I would definitely stay at this hotel again (also about the hotel there is a safe in the room which is also a bonus).  
<Date>Dec 1, 2006

<Author>Terese&Elena
<Content>Great littel hotel, great location I'm so glad I trusted the Trip Advisor reviews--this hotel is a gem. We decided rather last minute to take a Thanksgiving weekend trip to New York, so I was pleasantly surprised to be able to find a hotel in a great location at such a reasonable price for NYC ($220/nite for a regular double). The rooms wasn't huge by US standards, but was very well-maintained, smartly appointed, comfortable and, above all, clean! The doorman gave great tips and directions.The only funkiness is the minibar system, which is on a sensor and registers anything that's moved. <Author>Bmth
<Content>Fab Hotel First time in New York and we stayed at the Hotel Metro. Really centralised and from our room we could see Macy's. The room was a decent size and clean although the bathroom was a bit on the small side. There isn't any tea/coffee facilities in the room although you can get tea/coffee from the dining area 24 hrs a day. The breakfast is good: cereals, toast, muffins, croissants etc - enough to keep you going. Very comfortable dining area with two televisions. The staff at the hotel are very pleasant and helpful. They are happy to help you with working out the subway stops and recommending restaurants - try Phinos Italian restaurant - it's great! Unfortunately the rooftop terrace was closed for repairs so we didn't get to go up there which was a shame. We throughly enjoyed our stay here and would definitely stay again. It's situated in a great place close to the shops and the Empire State Building. It's about a 15-20 min walk to the Rockefeller Centre and Times Square. We would definitely recommend a stay here.

<Author>MisterBen
<Content>Great Hotel that is central to everything ! My partner and I stayed at The Metro from Saturday 4th November 2006 to Wednesday 8th November 2006. We were celebrating our 13th anniversary and went to NYC to do some sight seeing and shopping.This was my first visit to NYC and my partner's second visit.We had a superior deluxe room (407) which was bigger than anticipated as we thought rooms in New York were typically small; this was not the case at The Metro. We got 2 five foot beds, a large TV, minibar, dresser, table, coffee table, chairs, walk in wardrobe, safe, iroining board with quality iron that does not ruin you favourite shirts. The furniture was all walnut inlay and had a tasteful art-deco theme with pictures reminiscent of the film metropolis.The bathroom was also large and airy with Marble and Travetine decor. There were no issues with the water pressure.Breafast (included) consisted of a large selection of continental food and beverages. The Staff were very helpful and not in your face.On several occasions we found the front of house staff very helpful and receptive when we needed advice on the best way to get to places in and around the city. They were consistently helpful and friendly throughout our stay. They even supplied an umbrella on our last day when it rained so we did not get wet on our last shopping spree.The hotel is particulary well located because it is central to Manhatten, with Macy's, the world's biggest Footlocker, Victoria's Secret's, The Empire State Building and a variety of good jewellers very close (0 to 2 blocks). Everything else is a very short trip by foot or cab. The Hotel Bar makes a mean Apple or Strawberry Martini - make sure you try one even if you don't stay here !We also ventured out of town to Woodbury Common for the shopping which is just a bus ride away from the port authority which is a short cab ride or walk from the hotel. Time square is a short walk away as well.Favourite eat out was the Blue Fin on Union Square, again, just a short cab trip away from this centrally located hotel.All round, The Metro represents excellent value for money if you are on business or pleasure that is very centrally located within Manhattan with very tasteful clean rooms with good facilities and helpful staff.I will definitely be returning to this hotel on my next visit to Manhattan; loved the hotel, loved the people, loved New York.

<Content>Good value and great location. <Author>Bratz24
<Content>Great location, very friendly staff. I have just spent 5 days at the Hotel Metro with my 16 year old daugher and her friend. The location of the hotel was excellent for both sightseeing and shopping. We could walk everywhere we wanted to go. - Times Square 10 mins, 5th Avenue Shopping 15 mins, Empire State Building 2 mins! The room was very clean and had everything you could ask for, hairdryer, tv, minibar, iron and very comfortable beds. Breakfast was included and this was a great bonus as it meant we didn't have to look for somewhere to eat each morning. There was huge selection of muffins, bagels, cereals - in fact everything you could ask for. The hotel bar was very welcoming, food there was great too. Staff couldn't have been more helpful. I would recommend this hotel as an excellent choice for a short break. One tip though, ask for a room at the back of the hotel, ours was at the back and although there was no view, we also didn't have to listen to the traffic all night! I imagine rooms at the front could be a bit noisy.

<Content>Perfect for the occasion This hotel fitted the bill perfectly. Brilliant location, could not have asked for more. Quiet, clean and polite. <Author>Mia1976
<Content>Will stay there again My husband and I stayed at the Hotel Metro for 6 nights in August. We had booked it because of the good reviews on Tripadvisor. We had spent a long time trying to decide where to stay. But we are very happy we made this decision. We requested a room on the higher floors and got one just below the rooftop and it was really nice. I think it was a new room. My husband also told them it was my birthday and they had left some chocolates in the room. This hotel is great value for money. The breakfast is good. You get tea, coffee, fruit, bagels, toast, pastries and muffins. Enough to last you until lunchtime!The location is great too! It got Fifth Avenue on one side and Macy on the other. Times Square is only 5 minutes away. I definitely recommend doing the bus hop-on-hop-off thing. As you get unlimited rides for 72 hours we used the bus to go downtown for dinner as well. Saved us on paying for the underground or a taxi.There was one girl in reception who was a bit moody but the rest were helpful enough. I also used the beauty salon and the lady who runs it is really lovely. I had to wait for my nail polish to dry and she told me lots about her life in America. She originally from Romania.Also opposite the hotel a bit further down towards Fifth Avenue, there is a delicatessen store run by a Korean woman. At the back there is a little restaurant type thing which is amazing. My husband and I have lived in Hong Kong and are usually really fussy about our Chinese food but this was really good.All in all it was a good experience. The hotel is clean, good value for money and in a great location. I would definitively recommend it.

<Author>zski
<Content>Great for the price! I stayed at Hotel Metro over the last weekend. Even after reading the raving reviews, I was a bit skeptical since I had received such a low price (about $160/night, due to a special Sunday night discount). <Author>getzklein
<Content>Another great review We booked our stay at Hotel Metro based on the positive reviews we saw on Trip Advisor. All of the hotels in NYC were expensive when we were going and its hard to know which hotels are actually worth the money. I can honestly say that Hotel Metro was everything that we expected. It wasn't a luxurious hotel and I wasn't blown away, but it was exactly what we wanted and nothing was lacking.The location was great, walking distance to everything but not right in the middle of the Times Square craziness. The free breakfast was convenient and we found the staff to be helpful. The rooms were actually roomy, which I think is rare in the city. This was one of the few hotels where I could actually get a king size bed and be guaranteed a non smoking room. That to me was the worth the price. We requested an upper level floor room to cut down the traffic noise and we were given a room on the 12th floor, perfect. I would recommend this hotel to a friend.

<Author>SueMunn
<Content>What a view! This hotel is absolutely perfect. From check-in to check-out we could not have asked for more perfect service. Anu ,the concierge, is the most delightful person and she will do all in her power to make your stay memorable. Matthew on the door is always ready with a smile and helpful hints. Hotel is ideally situated for everything. Subway just at the end of the street; Macy's on the corner and the hotel provides maps, details of excursions and also a voucher to get discount on food at The Playright Irish Bar just a couple of doors away. The deck on top of the penthouse is an excellent way to spend a couple of hours just gazing at the Empire State Building. Bar on deck opens in good weather from 5pm - 10pm. Ice machine on top floor if you want to have drinks in your room. Have read in previous reviews that the staff are arrogant - don't know who wrote this but this definitely is not true. The complimentary breakfast is wonderful. Every type of bagel, muffins, fresh fruit, yoghurts, toast, coffee, tea, juice. Sets you up for all the walking you'll do!! Definitely visit O'Hara's bar at Ground Zero. Paul (owner's son) has a photo album of the aftermath of the tragedy which virtually decimated the bar. He is fantastic and we think he should be Prime Minister of the UK !! When you talk to him you'll see why!! His stories will make you laugh and cry - what a fantastic guy. The whole experience was wonderful. Definitely will go back.

<Author>Haywhitmom
<Content>Hidden Treasure! My daughter, upon turning 21, wanted to go to NYC to celebrate her new adulthood! I researched through TripAdvisor and decided on Hotel Metro. I was a little afraid that it could not live up to it's wonderful reviews but I am here to tell you that we LOVED the hotel. It is in a great location. Right down from a subway entrance and very close to bus lines and right across the street from the NY Empire State Bldg. We were a family of four so we opted for the Family Suite. Awesome! We had two bedrooms, very nice size, and a decent sized bathroom (large shower only) - Room 902! We could see the Empire State Bldg from our room. The patio on the roof is wonderful. We never saw them serving food or drinks from the roof but you could order from the Lobby Grill and take upstairs. We would go to the roof every night before bed just to take in the city lights. The continental breakfasts offered were very good. My only suggestion to them would be to add a microwave to warm up the pastries. We initially were so tempted to stay in a large hotel by Grand Central station and even another hotel by Times Square which was highly recommended but again I was so impressed by the reviews here that I went with Hotel Metro. I am so glad I resisted the GC hotel and VERY glad I did not stay any where closer to Times Square. We enjoyed our four nights, in our very clean quiet room and will definitely stay there again. I felt very safe there during the day AND at night ! Our only interaction with the front desk was at check-in where they were efficient but just a tad unfriendly. However, the lady who cleaned our room was very nice and friendly and very responsive when we asked for additional towels. We loved the hotel AND the city!

<Author>Dapster1920
<Content>Comfortable, cost effective and cozy! My 13-yr old neice chose this hotel from several others I had selected from many, many internet travel services. She made an excellent choice. The hotel is in a good and safe location (important for 3 women) and the staff was good. We asked and got a room (7th floor) in the back so the earplugs we brought along were not necessary. Once we got our location bearings, we walked! The Empire State Building is a block away, Macy's is across the street, Bloomingdales is a 20-minute walk and Central Park and the Met Museum is up Fifth Avenue-about a 45 minute walk. There are 2 good restaurants walking North for breakfast. Go to the ESB around 8am and you will be admitted quickly; otherwise, you will be in a long wait line. Also dine at the Grand Central Terminal at the Oyster Bar Restaurant. The bad part is that they are closed on Sundays. Overall, the Hotel Metro is a wonderful choice for the money, location, free breakfast and advice on food tips. I am going back to NYC for more sight seeing. Do not feel scared (especially if you are a female and traveling solo). Just orient yourself to the street grid and be aware of your surroundings and you will be fine.

<Author>BigTazNI
<Content>Two Star Hotel? - I don't think so!!! We stayed at the Metro from 30th June to 4th July 2006 and it was excellent. There were 11 in our party and we needed three family rooms and had problems booking them on-line but after a quick call to the hotel reservation staff who were excellent it was sorted very quickly and the rooms confirmed.When we arrived albeit late afternoon our rooms were ready for us. I could rant and rave about location which is excellent but most of New York is close to something instead lets talk about where you will spend the night after a long day sightseeing or shopping. The family rooms we had were spacious not by New York standards but by any hotel standards. Our room had a bathroom with a superb powerful shower that always had hot water. There was a separate room with a King bed for the adults and there were two queen size beds in the main living area for the kids. There were two TV's, one per room, an adequate fridge to chill drinks in and access to an ice maker on the 12th (penthouse) floor. Speaking of the 12th floor, up here there is a good gym, if you are keen, but the jewel in the crown has to be the roof garden where you can relax at the end of the day with friends, a cold drink, and look up at the neighbours across the street on the Empire State Building!!! Each room has an air con unit which I suppose are loud but not so that you get annoyed and during our nights in the hotel you certainly needed them to keep the rooms cool. The hotel supplies a breakfast in the morning and even over the holiday weekend (the hotel was full) there were plenty of seats and loads to eat (albeit that the ladies in charge had to re-stock a few times), bagels, muffins, bread (toaster also), croissants, cereals, tea, coffee, and fruit juices. Breakfast sets you up for the day ahead. Tea and coffee is available free all day for hotel guests. I have seen some complaints about lifts but they were fine and any dealings we had with staff proved their worth. Noise wise, it is New York where car horns have to wear out before tyres, so get used to a bit of noise at night the city never sleeps. My wife and I stayed in the Metro 21/2 years ago and whilst the hotel was good then it is even better now as most rooms have been refurbished and they are finishing the 7th floor at the momentI suppose at 150 per night it might have been regarded as expensive but well woth the money considering location, room, and breakfast and tha fact that you can have up to five people per family room.

<Author>HoustonTripper
<Content>Great location, wifi, free breakfast I just returned from a 5 day stay at Hotel Metro and here are my opinions:Positives- Free breakfast (includes 3-4 cereals, many kinds of muffins and bagels), not hot- Location, literally 50 paces from subway entrance.- Free wifi worked extremely well from my room and the cafe.Negatives- Room was small but knowing this going in, it wasn't a big deal.- Street noise was pretty bad. <Content>Fantastic hotel and great staff My husband and I went to New York with my old school friend and her partner - originally we were going to celebrate mine and my friend's 50th birthdays - however our friends decided that whilst we were there they would get married at Central Park. From the day we arrived at the hotel we could not fault the service we got. The staff were absolutely great, especially James and Jetto, who helped us with the wedding arrangements. James recommend a restaurant for our friends wedding night and Jetto arranged for champagne and room upgrades (my daughter had e-mailed the hotel to let them know of our friends wedding). The hotel was very clean and the rooms were comfortable. There was a sun terrace you could go to and the bar was open there in the evening. Location could not have been better - we were 2 minutes from Maceys which my friend and I made the most of and visited there every day - 5 minutes from Empire State Building (make sure you go at night - view breathtaking) - 10 minutes from Time Square and 2 seconds from Metro. The people in New York were so friendly. The wedding in Central Park was fantastic and everything went without a hitch. We would also most certainly go back again and in fact have made a pact to go back in 5 years time to celebrate our friends anniversary.

<Author>Gil1018
<Content>Very Nice Hotel I will say that the hotel was nice. The only thing negative I have to say is that the neighborhood around the hotel leaves something to be desired. We arrived from Penn Station about 9PM. We walked about 3 blocks to the hotel. On the block that the hotel is located, there are several small restaurants. Each of these restaurants had put out their trash for pickup right about the time we arrived. Not only was there about 100 plastic bags of trash, the smell was tremendous. There is enough foot traffic at that hour so that I didn't feel unsafe. Macy's is right down the street as well as major subway and bus lines. And of course, Penn Station. I stayed here one night because of its proximity to Penn Station and the LIRR/Airtrain to JFK airport. The trip to the airport using the public transportation was $10. By cab, it would have cost over $50 with tip. The city caps cab fares but only from the airport to Manhattan. Going to the airport, it's let the buyer beware. Would stay again.

<Author>Janet Beadle
<Content>Good Hotel We stayed at the Metro Hotel for 2 nights prior to our cruise and for 1 night after our cruise in December 2005. We liked the Art Deco feel of the Hotel  think it was reasonable value for a New York Hotel.Both the rooms we had were fine, but as we expected quite small however, we were able to store the luggage we didn't need in the luggage room.There was no problem with noise as on both occasions our room were on the higher floors.We thought the extras like the constant tea /coffee was great when we arrived in from the cold and the buffet breakfast was good. Being able to use the facility to check in on line for our flights and print off our boarding pass was useful.The reception staff were helpful and managed to get us transport to JFK despite there being a transport strike and the price was much cheaper than Cunard the Cruise line would have charged us in normal circumstances.On balance we think the Metro Hotel is a good choice if you are realistic about what you get for you money in terms of accommodation in New York.

<Author>Rob&Sieran
<Content>Great location, good hotel Having stayed at the Metro I can agree with almost all the comments made previously. What I would say is if you are going to New York to stay in a plush hotel then you may be disappointed with the Metro. If you are going to New York to get out and about, see all the sites all day and night and simply crash out exhausted then the Metro is ideally located and will suit your needs. The breakfast is great and will set you up for the day. If you arrive at daft o'clock there is a deli just up from the hotel and bars/restaurants almost opposite and down the street.We stayed at the Metro end of May beginning of June 2006 as it was our honeymoon I was obviously concerned. If you were like us more excited about visiting New York and only sleeping etc in the hotel then you should be fine. We were on the fourth floor at the back, at this level with it being Manhattan the room was a little dark, however what else would you expect surrounded by other tall buildings?When we needed information from the front desk yes it was a hit and miss affair, but again what isn't? For us there was far more to see and do in New York to worry about our room. Don't get me wrong though if it was damp, mouldy and smokey I would have asked to be moved and would have been annoyed if we couldn't move.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Disappointed During a recent visit to NYC, I stayed at the Hotel Metro for one night. Overall, I was not impressed. The Hotel itself is located on a narrow street in the Garment District. I got a room on the third floor and it was incredibly noisy ---- all night. Car alarms, trash pickup and people on the street were some of the sounds I heard before finally falling asleep. The rooms were smaller than average, with my room being half the size of the room I stayed at in the Affinia Dumont. There were two single beds, which is not what my wife and I had in mind when we booked the room. The bellhop was basically useless, except for storing bags. While this hotel is cheap, you can do much better in NYC for just a little more money.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Loved the Hotel Metro and Staff My daughter and I recently returned form a trip to NYC and the Hotel Metro. The hotel itself is beautiful, well-appointed and most importantly centrally located. Macy's, the Empire State Building, Times Square, Theater District, Seventh Avenue, 5th Avenue, and Madison Ave are all within walking distance. If you want to venture further, the subway entrance is steps from the hotel entrance. Every day, my daughter and I would venture out to various places and along the way find additional NYC experiences within a block of the hotel. You can't beat the location.My first room was ok, but after my first day I asked for a room with a tub and with tact and patience recieved one. All rooms are beautiful but some are larger than others. Ask for a bay window room. Don't expect a view regardless but there is a beautiful rooftop terrace that offers a breathtaking view. The Metro offers a nice continental breakfast that continues until 11:00. As a result, my daughter and I normally only bought one additional meal per day. This left $$$ for all the great shopping available. On our last day there, I discovered all the great eateries around Time Square. They're a traveler's dream...Island food, Jersey Chicken, etc., for less than $5. I'll remember this on my next trip.Thanks to the wonderful staff, George and Jeto (front desk) and the breakfast staff, we'll definitely be back. Every day they graciously mapped out our destinations, gave insider tips and sent us out feeling welcomed and supported. Thanks George and Jeto. Unfortunately, one bad note. The bellman called a NYC taxi for us as we were leaving for LaGuardia. The taxi was supposed to cost$22. The taxi charged us $36 because he said he had to wait for us. Who asked him to wait? Anyway, that's the beauty of Hotel Metro. You don't have to deal with taxis, because everything is within walking distance. An added bonus: get on the Metro 1 or 3 and get a wonderful tour from Central Park to famous Madison or 5th for $2.Again, we loved the Metro and we loved the staff. See ya in October.  
<Date>May 29, 2006

<Author>Elke V
<Content>Liked the hotel very much We (50, 50, 20, and 15) spent five days in New York and especially the Hotel Metro.There were several other Dutch families in the hotel, next to the many Americans.Our rooms were rooms at the streetside of the hotel (not the lately renovated ones). Next time we would ask for a room at the backside, because we heard those were much quieter. Our sons had difficulties sleeping that well with the carbage trucks which frequented the street every night. But: they got used to it at the end of the week. But nevertheless: the rooms were very tidy and well cleaned.The breakfast was very good and you could eat as much as you wanted. It was also possible to drink coffee 24 hours a day.A great plus was the rooftop: for people who wanted to smoke as well as for people wanting to sit in the sun for some time.Hotel Metro, 35th street (near Macy's) was a great starting point for our American sightseeing trips. You could either walk (even walking to Central Park was ok) or take the metro. We didn't go by bus, because the streets were so crowded. The Metro was much quicker.We liked New York very much and think about coming back within a couple of years. There were so many interesting things to watch and the whole atmosphere was great.Elke V.

<Content>Good value compared with other hotels in area I stayed here my first trip to NYC in december. <Author>destined2travel
<Content>Hotel Metro We stayed at the Hotel Metro from 29th December for 7 nights, over new year. Having been to New York the previous Feb, we were very excited to be staying more central (pretty much on the same street as Macy's). The hotel has a great location, 10/15 min walk to Time Square and Madison Square Garden and a couple of blocks from the Empire State Building.There was a little confusion over rates when we arrived but all was sorted in the morning, and the staff could not apologise enough.The complimentary breakfast consisted of bagels, muffins, toast etc, which was a great start to the day. The hotel itself i very retro, although we didn't spend that much time in the hotel really, generally out about 9/10am every morning and back about 6pm to get ready for whatever we had planned for the evening.Being our second visit, we didn't do as many touristy things this time round, although we did the the Empire State Building again, you cannot beat the views.We saw our 2nd Knicks game at the Garden, very exciting just being there, i'm not a basketball fan (Boyfriend is) but I found myself enjoying it and really getting into it.Had a very wet but amazing NewYear in Times Square, I can't even begin to describe the atmosphere being there at that time. It is definitely something everyone should experience once in their lifetime. Although saying that I don't know if I would want do it again, just because it's a memory that is best left unspoilt. I think once you've done it, it wouldn't be the same the next time.There are plenty of great restaurants around and we were lucky enough to stumble across a a couple that seemed unknown to tourists and were great value for money. I still haven't seen a Broadway show, but that is definitely on the itinery for next time. There is so much to do and see in New York you probably wouldn't ever get everything done, even if you had a lifetime. New York is so magical and amazing and it is absolutely the best city in the world and after 2 trips we are now planning our 3rd for next Feb.If you haven't been, go, you won't regret it!!!!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>The Best Small Hotel In New York We Stayed in the Hotel Metro on our very first trip to New York. As with any first visit to a new city we were concerned if the hotel would be nice. This was a fantastic hotel to stay in and it has all the amenities you would need. I travelled with my parents so we booked a family suite which consists of two double beds in the main room, one other bed in another room, one bathroom and a small area with a fridge and a sink. There was one wardrobe in the main room but plenty of drawers in each of the rooms. There is also a television in each room and a safe in the wardrobe.There is a complimentary breakfast every morning in the hotel. The choice is very good and includes cereals, toast, frsh fruit, begals and muffins. There is also tea and coffee available 24 hours a day which is perfect after a day walking around the cityThe hotel is in a perfect location. it is situated midtown and it is only a street away from the Empire State Building which we could see from our window and the roof top terrace (open seasonally). Times Square is only a 10 minute walk away in which there are good restaurants and shops. We ate in the hard rock cafe whcih was very good- it looks as if it is just a shop but the restaurant is downstairs. We tried the bus tour around the city - the ticket is valid for 48 hours and it a great idea to help you find your way around the city. We also did the 3 hour island cruise which is run through Circle Line (pier 83). This cruise is excellent and you get a very good close view of the statue of liberty. The Rockefeller Centre is worth a vist especially top of the rock - an observatory deck. The view is similar to the Empire State building but sligtlty better as it includes a good view of central park. The park is also a must to do - we spent 2 days there as there is plenty to do and if the weather is good it is nice to sit and watch the world go by. Some restaurants we went to which i recommend are:-Sevilla Restaurant 62 Charles Street, Greenwich Village. This is a spanish restaurant with a mixture of tapas and other traditional spanish dishes. The staff are very friendly and the food is excellent. Spend some nights in Greenwich Village as there are great restaurants. Another one which we had a good meal in was Bistecca Fiorentina Steak which is on 317 west 46th Street. This is on restaurant Row which has a good chocie of different restaurants. We also went to the View Restaurant (New York's only Revolving restaurant) in The Marriott Hotel Times Square. the food was not very good and not worth the money but the view was amazing. I would recommend go for a drink and not dinner - this is a view not to be missed!Overall I highly recommend that you visit New York and stay at the wonderful Hotel Metro!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Location ... OK Hotel My Partner and I stayed at the Metro Hotel for ten days in late March. The first thing we noticed as we stepped out of the cab with our luggage was no bell boys. The entrance features two double glass doors with a couple of steps. Keeping those doors open and lugging bags was a little tricky.We found that the reception desk were a little rude, often talking amongst themselves, first when we were checking in and secondly when we had to call them. I didn't feel the hotel had an atmosphere or vibe like many others i've experienced in NYC. I feel it is better suited to families and older couples.We had a large room with a window out to the street, if you're a light sleeper (like me) than ask for a room in the back section as the noise and the rubbish trucks does filter through. The decor of the hotel is in need for a touch up or revamp and not to our taste. Breakfast menu was great, and the all day coffee was convenient.Location was great for shopping, empire state building, a couple blocks from madison square garden and about 6ish blocks away from Times Square. Overall, we wouldn't stay at Hotel Metro again, there are better hotels in NYC for about the same price.

We were also able to check in early which was great as we were able to freshen up before hitting 5th avenue! Location is superb;everything is walkable, even Central Park and Brooklyn Bridge! We could not find fault with anything and would not use any other hotel if we're lucky enough to come back . Enjoy!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Value and Service After reading the mixed reviews for the Metro, we weren't sure what we were going to see when we arrived. The staff was awesome when it came to giving us directions and were always friendly. It was moderately priced, and the food was great.Our room was clean and quiet. We expected a VERY small room from the reviews posted here, but we had plenty of room. Who visits NY to stay in their room anyhow? The location of the hotel felt very safe. You're in the heart of the action - only 2 blocks to Madison Square Garden, and about 5 blocks from Times Square. You can walk anywhere in midtown from here. And there's a subway stop across the street in front of Macy's. The only regret we have is that we went before the rooftop bar had opened - I bet it is lovely in the summer. We took advantage of it to take some cool photos of the Empire State Bldg though.Again on our departure day, the hotel staff stored our bags after we checked out so that we could enjoy the city without carrying them. I would recommend this hotel to friends and family. In fact - I already have!

<Author>scotfree
<Content>Lovely Hotel I booked the Hotel metro on a friend's recommendation and have been recommending it to folk since I got back. We had booked a normal Queen sized room but got upgraded to a double Queen. Not sure if this was because we had told them we were there to get married but if I was going back I'd want the same kind of room again as it was lovely and other reviews suggest that the smaller rooms are quite tiny. The beds were very comfy, plenty pillows and everything was spotless. Other reviews have said that rooms at back of hotel and on higher floors are the best, and that is where our room was and it was indeed quiet (I think this was the quietest hotel I have stayed in, not what you expect in the middle of Manhattan).Staff were polite although not overly friendly, apart from the Hungarian woman on the desk who got very excited about us getting married. I think the 'attitude' is just New York, we found far worse examples of it in certain shops - Macy's being by far the worst.Location wise we couldn't fault it, Subway station,buses, Macy's (if you like that kind of thing), Victorias Secret, Gap all at end of road in one direction, Empire State right there, and only 10-15 minutes walk up to Times Square and Central Park.Complimentary breakfast was fine for us, we had expected to go out for breakfast but we enjoyed the huge muffins, pastries and bagels, with some healthy cereal, fruit and yoghurt to start.We didn't expect to use the internet room, but since our mobile didn't work after the first day we ended up using it alot, and had no problems getting access, they didn't seem too strict about the 30 minute limit either, as long as no-one was wanting the key.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>highly recommended My wife and I stayed at the Metro in mid-March. Location is great, walkable from Penn Station even with luggage, even at night. Our room was large for NY, clean and comfortable. Our room faced the street and there was some street noise, but it didn't keep us up. There was a bit of noise from the adjoining room, but not intrusive. The breakfast is good quality, with bagels and muffins from a bakery, fresh coffee, and a clean and comfortable dining area. We took advantage of free internet, computer and printer in the business center (20 minute limite, and sometimes a wait in the morning). There is a Duane Reade and a green grocer within 2 blocks, both of which we took advantage of. We ate at the Korean restaurant next door (open all night) late one night and found that food to be good as well. We booked this through Orbitz for $150 per night just a day in advance of our trip, and at that rate this was an extremely good deal.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Location, kocation, location I stayed at the Metro 11 years ago, The location is second to none, slap bang in the thick of it, Macy's to the right, 5th Avenue to the left, perfect and this was the deciding factor for a return trip to the Metro. I was disappointed with the decoration of the hotel; it was shall we say tired and clearly hasn't had a touch up since my last trip. Having said that, the rooms were spotless, and cleaned every day. We were on the 12th floor with a great view of the Empire States. We had 2 double beds in our room; the bathroom was big with red hot water, a big cupboard for our clothes and cases and a safe. The fridge came in handy but it was very noisy in the night. We didn have breakfast in the hotel instead we went out, we found a great place called Jimmy on 6th Avenue serving a huge variety of hot foods, which set us up for the day. The Metro promotes Brendon Bar which is opposite the hotel; I would NOT recommend this place at all, and I suggest the Metro remove their association. The staff and service was appalling, we were made to feel grateful for getting a drink. After sitting us down at a table, it was apparent that the diners around us were not satisfied, so we decided to pay for our drinks and leave. We had a great meal in the Metro Grill next to the hotel instead. I would definitely stay at the Metro again but would hope theye had a bit of a refurb by then!
