When we got into the room, we found it was on the first floor facing the road. (brilliant!!). As this was a special trip for my Girlfriend, I decided to stay where we were and see how it went (instead of making a fuss and asking to be moved). In the end, it didn't matter too much as we were never in the room and I only got woken up a couple of time by traffic outside (your so tired with working all day - you sleep through anything!).The Room was a good size, with the decoration good taste. Also included was a fridge and Safe, which both came in handy during our stay. The bathroom was of a good standard, although the toilet did overflow once....although the maid cleared it up within half an hour which was good.Breakfast was 1st class and settled the day up well. Could have as much as you want, ranging from muffins, toast, fruit and cakes. We often went back time and time again for a refill!!Location is the best part of this Hotel. 10 minute walk to Times Square and 2 minutes to Macys! (which my Girlfriend loved!). The Subway is around a minute walk also, which gives you access to the rest of the City.Free Internet access (although limited to 30 mins) was handy and we used it several times for booking an excursion for during our stay.The Roof Top Terrace was nice and I can imagine in the Summer being popular.Overview:You get what you pay for. We enjoyed our stay at the Hotel and found it exactly what we wanted. Would we stay here again? Maybe. First would look for what else was available. All in all though, was worth the money I paid.  
<Date>Mar 3, 2006

<Author>Isidore
<Content>Expensive for what it delivers This hotel does not live up to some of the rave reviews I read on this site and it is expensive for what it delivers. The rooms are adeqaute but old-fashioned, bordering on the shabby. Nobody at the front desk advised me on arrival that there was a free breakfast, and I therefore did not avail of it - indeed these staff, though not discourteous, are not exactly pro-active. The exception is the excellent hall-porter, who is cheerful and efficient and who was coping splendidly with the conditions of Great Blizzard of February 2006. Free Broadband access is only through two terminals in the business centre and users are limited to 30 minutes per session - very inconvenient for anybody needing longer access for business communication purposes. I will not be coming back to this hotel, despite its central location.

<Content>Loved the Metro I stayed at the Metro at the end of November 05 while on a 4 day shopping trip with my mother. The location of the hotel could not be better. One street away from the Empire State Building and Macy's just down the street.....Excellent! Also, with the subway literally a minute's walk away at the corner of the street, you could be at your next destination within minutes.The hotel itself was above average for what is classed as a 2/3 star hotel. The decor in the lobby was lovely - I really liked the art deco style. The free breakfast (bagels/cereal/muffins/toast/fruit/yoghurt/danish pastry) was fantastic too - and really set you up for a day of sightseeing and shopping! And the all day free tea/coffee was great aswell. Overall we were delighted with our stay in the Metro. The hotel staff were always friendly, pleasant and very helpful with any queries we had. I would undoubtedly stay at the Hotel Metro again, and have already recommended it to several friends!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Good hotel, Great location! My first time in NYC and was really happy with the hotel i picked. Maceys is on the doorstep which is great when you have lots of bags to carry!! Small, yet friendly hotel and the free breakfast in the morning is really handy, offering toast,yogurts, cereal, muffins and bagels etc etc. Also, free tea and coffee all day every day.Rooms were spacious with a good sized bathroom and double shower, and the rooms had maid service every day. (new towels fresh sheets every day).Our room faced onto the main road so early hours of the morning was noisy when refuge collectors came round (for example!)Just over a five minute walk to time square but central park was a good twenty minutes away-not appreciated in freezing cold temperatures!!(so get a taxi) Most of the hotel staff were friendly, although didn't go the extra mile! Also close by was a cinema and american eateries for evenings out.For those who like Maceys, if you go to the welcome desk you will get a discount voucher which you can use in conjunction with any other discounts that they have at the time! Other tips for those that like to see musicals........ Go to the TICKET booth in Time Square for 3pm and you can get upto 50% off shows for that evening, although i would suggest getting there abit before 3 as the queues can be very long (we queued for 1hr 30mins but well worth it)Would definetly recommend this hotel for those seeking a good hotel in a fab location!!

<Content>Great location Stayed at Hotel Metro from Dec 19 to 22 2005. Like most people we chose this hotel because of Tripadvisor reviews and couldn't have been happier. We have teens aged 15 and 17 so had requested interconnecting rooms which we were given. Although the twin room was bigger both it and the double room were a great size, with plenty of room for a dresser, large bedside tables plus a fridge and a table and two chairs. Bathrooms were very clean with huge showers. The decor was very art deco. As we were only on the third floor bit noisy at night but then this city really never sleeps! The complimentary breakfast was a great bonus and the public areas all very nice. We had tickets for NY Rangers ice hockey at MSG and Spamalot and both were within a 5-10 minute walk, as was Empire State Building and our favourite shop Macys. Would definitely stay here again!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great location, great staff We were in NYC during the transit strike. The Hotel Metro turned out to be the best location for going uptown and downtown. Travelled w/ husband and 17 and 19 year old kids. Got the family suite. A little pricey but  NYC is pricey. Great to have a breakfast right there so we Floridians didn't need to freeze our buns off to get a cup of coffee or cocoa in the morning. The doorman is worthy of extra praise and a big tip when you leave. He was pleasant, helpful and kind. They gave us room 1002 and one room had a view of Herald Square and the lights at Macy's and the other room had a view of the Empire State building. NYC tips- I emailed MTV several months prior to arrival and got my kids tix to be in the audience. At Christmas they give all audience members a free gift. They got new digital cameras. Within walking distance (15 minutes) on 2nd ave and 35th is a diner called the Gemini Diner. I read a review on menu pages and thought we'd check it out. My kids could care less about fancy restaurants and I hate chains. It was reasonable priced , had awesome food and a huge selection. And homemade desserts. We walked alot, spent alot but had a fantastic time.

<Author>lma13
<Content>Loved Hotel Metro! I was pretty confident in booking the Hotel Metro after reading reviews on this site. However, I just got back from my stay in NYC, and I was amazed with this hotel. For the price of $147 a night (on expedia), you can't beat this hotel. The lobby is nice, it has a restaurant and a bar, and the continental breakfast and the room it was in was great. Our room was surprisingly big, especially considering NYC hotel standards. It was spotless, including the bathroom and refidgerator. As for location, we were interested in seeing Times Square, Rockefellar Center, and a musical in the theatre district. We were able to walk to all of these places from the hotel (especially considering the transit strike while we were there) within 12 minutes. It is in a great location, the street it is on has several restaurants, and you can see Macy's/Herald Square from just outside the front entrance. Overall, this hotel is amazing for its price range and I would recommend it to anyone.

<Author>gemski_b
<Content>Wow! Right in the centre of NYC. Excellent hotel. I'm sorry if this review looks long but we had such a good time here I want every one to know how great it was. As this hotel was fantastic. I have recently got back from New York with my boyfriend. We were there for 5 nights from 3rd dec to 8th dec and had an absolutely superb time here. From the moment we stepped off the plane the people were so friendly. This made us feel very welcome and completely at ease. We took the New Jersey transit train from Newark airport to Penn station which is known to be faster to get in to the city than taxis and air shuttles. Only took around 20 minutes and cost $14 each. Then from Penn station it is only a 5 minute walk to the hotel, not worth getting a taxi, and you will not look out of place with a suitcase as not many people care. They are busy going about their own business! When we got into the hotel the guy on the desk was really friendly as were all the people in the hotel. The room wasn't huge but you won't need it to be any bigger if you're here for shopping and sight seeing. There is a fantastic roof terrace which is open all year round but the bar on the roof is only open in the summer. You will have a fantastic view of the Empire State building where you will get superb views.The continental breakfast was also a great bonus as it means you can fill up before doing the sights without worring about where to eat. The breakfast was a choice of cereals, gorgeous bagels, toast, fruit salad, yogurts, fruit juices, muffins the size of your hand, pastries, fruit and tea and coffee. You will definately be filled up by the breakfast as you can eat as much as you like. The hotel is within walking distance of the Empire State Building, Macys, Times Square, Central Park, lots of restaurants, Bloomingdales, FAO Swartz and Broadway theatres. Central Park takes bout 15mins to walk to but well worth it as it saves on cost of taxis which can be slow because of traffic and can work out pricey. I won't go on for too much longer but make sure you book a return to the airport as getting back to airports in a taxi run on the meter and are expensive and may not be available.The food in O'Neils steakhouse was fantastic, never tasted lamb so juicy and perfect, but is a little more expensive but well worth it for the great food and service also if you get the new york pass you get 20% discount.We are already planning our trip back here next year that's how good it is, you don't need to look any further than the hotel metro, it's safe and comfy and clean.If you would like any more info on NYC then feel free to email me and I will try to help. My email address is gemski_b@hotmail.com and title it with trip advisor query and i will get back to you as soon as possible.Oh and go and see The Lion King show on broadway it was amazing, you can normally book seats at the theatre on the day but for normal prices, don't expect to find any discounts for this show as it is too popular. Also avoid The Producers show, it is said to be hilarious but we found it boring and not funny. You can get cheap tickets from the TKTS booth in the centre of Times Square some at 50% discount. But check times of opening normally around 3 for evening shows and be prepared to stand in line for a while.One last tip, wrap up very warm its sooooo cold!!!!Well done for reading to the end ;o)Gemma.  
<Date>Dec 11, 2005

<Author>NUTTERCUP
<Content>Ideal location Just returned from a 4 night break in New York but feel like I need another holiday to get over this 1! The hotel is the ideal location for anyone wanting to explore all the tourist attractions. It is less than a minutes walk away from Macey's, 5 minutes from the Empire State Building and about 10 minutes walk away from Time Square. Central Park is about a 20 minute walk but theres so much to see along the way it goes really quick. I was actually surprised how near everything was to each other.We bought a Metro card and caught the bus to Ground Zero and the ferry to go to the Statue of Liberty. We didn't actually go onto Ellis Island but caught the free ferry to Staten Island and jumped straight back on to come back. It was a good way to get some great photos. We also caught the ferry in the evening to get some photos of New York by night. It was far from a relaxing break and by the 3RD day my feet were screaming for me to stop walking on them! The free breakfast was a great way to start the day. There was bagels, cereals, fresh fruit, toast, coffee(24 hours a day),tea, juices and muffins on offer. The only downside of the hotel was there wasn't a bath in the room although I'm told that most hotels only have showers so it seems that its not unusual but after all that walking all I wanted to do was have a relaxing soak in the bath. The roof top terrace was closed when we were there, apparently its closed for the season. The rooms are clean, comfortable and of a decent size but to be honest, you spend so little time in the room anyway!If you want to know anything else, just email me and I will try to be of some help!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Excellent New York Experience!! My experience at the Hotel Metro was awesome! Having stayed there in order to attend my sister's wedding, the location, atmosphere,  service was great. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great stay at the Metro Stopped at the Metro on our first visit to New York. Booked the hotel after reading good reviews on this site so thought it only fair to add our review. The first thing to say is that I would not hesitate to recommend this hotel. The location is perfect for tourists with all the sights within easy reach either on foot or via the subway at the end of the street. Macey's is also at the end of the street and Empire State Building around the corner. The hotel itself is just what you require, although on the small side the room was clean, bed comfortable, sufficient amenities (we did have a wardrobe !!) and the shower and bathroom were a good size. We too had an issue with the air conditioning with our unit not working on arrival however this was immediately attended to.As others have mentioned the breakfast and free tea and coffee was great with the later a very pleasant welcome after a long day sightseeing, making up for the lack of tea/coffee facilities in the room.The staff were very friendly, although we were faced with a frosty reception on our arrival after a long flight and fraught journey from the airport. In general though their helpful and friendly nature during our stay made up for this poor first impression. In summary, as I previously stated, I would not hesitate to recommend this hotel to anyone who is looking for a clean, friendly and comfortable base for their trip to New York.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Not a Bad Choice I was a little unsure of the hotel due to a number of negative reviews in Trip Advisor when I looked at the reviews early this summer. But the positive reviews made it sound good and it had all the amenities I was looking for. The end result was that I was pleased with the choice. Some of the problems may have been related to the ongoing remodeling. Our room was neat and clean and probably a good sized room for a mid-priced hotel - I have very little experience with New York hotels. Here's what I liked: The queen room was fairly spacious. The Continental breakfast was a whole lot more that the fat (making) muffins everyone has raved about - yogurt, mixed fruit, bagels, and cold cereal. Food was very well stocked except maybe cold cereal at the end of the morning. Exercise room was more than the usual couple of tread mills but not a whole lot more. Patio terrace. Central mid-town location within easy walking distance of all up-town/down-town subways and Penn station. Very nice and roomy bathroom. Front desk pleasant and helpful. Two computers for Internet access. Sometimes had to wait. The only negative - towels removed by housekeeping by mid-morning and not replace to afternoon. They were always at the Laundry.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>excellent value!! Save yourself the hours of on-line researching that I did. Just ante up at the Hotel Metro. I know it's difficult to think of $250 a night as a value, but wait until you see what you get elsewhere. I was very pleased with our stay there. I would highly recommend, though, going for one of the larger rooms. We got one of the small suites so that our daughter could have a room of her own. Her room alone was larger than the room we had at The Plaze for $350. One huge drawback. Turn right out of the hotel entrance, take a few steps west, and there's . . . Macy's! So if you're briinging your wife or teenage daughters, look out. Lucky for me, right at the end of the block was a terrific Italian deli, Giuseppe's. If I had the time, I would have ordered my way through the entire menu. There's also a little coffe shop right across the street. But get this . . . on our first morning there, I walked back into the hotel with one of those $5 bagels and a $3 cup of coffee . . . and there, rihjt off the lobby, is a wonderful buffet breakfast, compliments of the hotel! What an idiot!The staff at the front desk was rather cool and unhelpful, but the wait staff were all very sweet. Finally, take the elevator to the very top. There's a lovely open patio up there. During the day you can sun-bathe, so that the office workers in the Empire State Building next door can ogle you. And at night, check out the same scene, only now with a party crowd sampling the beer on top, on tap!The rooms are starkly post-modern, but in an artful way. Best of all they were clean. Have a Metrolicious stay!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Love the rooftop deck This hotel is reasonably priced and centrally located in Manhattan. The rooms are just big enough, with small marble baths, and a refrigerator. Don't hesitate to stay here. The deck is a quiet get-away spot in the middle of a hectic city.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A TERRIFIC Value The Hotel Metro exceeded our expectations!We were upgraded to a penthouse room that had two double beds (perfect, since I was traveling with a friend) and a sofabed. There were two sinks (one in the bathroom and one right outside), a shower and tub combination, a large TV with expanded cable, and a refrigerator. Although we were on the same floor as the rooftop bar, it was very quiet. The best aspects of the hotel were the beautiful condition of the rooms, the friendly desk staff, the free gym, the free internet access (the business center has two computers with high-speed internet), the free breakfast and the free weekday NY Times. That's a huge savings -- gyms can cost $15/day, breakfasts at least $10, and internet cafes cost time and money.My only complaint stemmed from when we tried to alter our reservation. At one point, we tried to come a day later, and they wouldn't change our reservation without raising our daily rate by 25%. We ended up with our original reservation, but if we had truly needed to come later, it would have been a big problem.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Decent Hotel in Nice Location The Metro Hotel is a nice hotel. It's definitely not a Ritz Carlton or Four Seasons but I can say that I didn't have any problems with it. Well, it's easy to find problems with any hotel if one looks hard enough. There were a few little things that were kind of strange, but definitely nothing bad or anything to be worried about. For example, one night one of the maids left one of her cleaning rags in our room. It looked like she had spilled something on the floor and tried to clean it up--and then left behind her rag (and part of the spill, too). It wasn't a big deal, we just threw the rag on the floor by the door and it was gone the next day. I'm sure if we had called the front desk that someone would have come cleaned up the spill (what was remaining of it) but it wasn't really a big deal. It was just kind of strange how it looked like something had spilled and then the maid tried to clean it up but then stopped and left and left behind her cleaning rags and things. Strange. Other than that, everything was fine with the hotel. The front desk staff seemed nice--not overly friendly--but still polite. The hotel had a great air conditioning unit in each room which was great since I was there in July. My friend  I would leave in the morning and not come back to the hotel until late at night and when we would come in, the air in our room would be on and the room was nice and cool and it felt SOOOO good. I got cold at times, though, but that wasn't a problem because you can control the temperature in the room, which is great. Also, some reviewers said they only had a shower in their rooms. I had a shower and a bathtub in my room, although I only used the shower. The water pressure/heat were fine. Again, it wasn't some fancy massaging showerhead that one would find in a 5-star hotel but it was your ordinary shower and it worked fine, so no complaints. I didn't really care for their shower products. They give you shampoo, conditioner, soap, and I think body lotion. They weren't bad or anything but I just preferred a different fragrance, so I just picked up some other shampoo/bodywash from Bath  Body Works. But, I wouldn't have any problem using the hotel's products. Usually my friend and I got up early but when we woke up I was surprised to already hear the maids in the hall cleaning up, but they didn't disturb us because we had the do not disturb sign on the door. So, we didn't have any problem with maids waking us up in the morning by coming in our room or anything (a problem I've had in some other hotels). Also, as some other people have mentioned, each room has a refrigerator in it. I love that! Most hotels these days will give you a minibar, charge you triple prices on everything, and then put up a sign that says don't put your own products in the minibar but it wasn't like that at all at the Metro Hotel. They give you your own fridge and there are lots of 24 hour drugstores and things around so you can buy your own food/drinks if you want to and put them in the fridge. My friend thought the fridge might make too much noise during the night but I don't think it did at all. I never heard it. Besides, if it did then you could always unplug it. We didn't really buy any food but it was nice to keep some drinks in the fridge so we could have something cold to drink whenever we wanted. Also, the hotel does have room service if you don't want to leave your room. Another plus is that the hotel has free wireless internet access. So, if you have a laptop then bring it with you. The signal strength wasn't the best for me but it was good enough to be able to hop online long enough to check your email and things like that. One concern that I had about the hotel is that the rooms do NOT have in-room safes. So I was worried about leaving my laptop in my room. But I did leave it in my room and didn't have any problem. However, the hotel does say that if you have valuables and don't want to leave them in your room, then you can leave them with the front desk and then pick them up later. If you can't/don't want to bring a laptop, then the hotel does have a business center with a computer/printer. There is also a small gym and a rooftop terrace/bar. I went inside the gym although I didn't really workout--I just wanted to see it. I went to the rooftop, too, but it was cloudy and at night and I couldn't really see anything, but I'm sure it would be nice during the day. It definitely gives you a good view of the Empire State Building. My room was on the 2nd floor and so most of the time I just took the stairs from the lobby but whenever I wanted to use the elevators, they were very fast and I didn't have to spend much time waiting. However, the elevators were always hot inside. I don't know why but geesh they were hot. but again, it's just a fast elevator, so I can't complain--it's not like I was sleeping in it, ha ha. Just going from floor 1 to floor 2, which too around 10 seconds, ha ha. I arrived at the hotel btwn 2pm-3pm and my room was ready right away. I didn't have to wait at all. As someone else mentioned, the bed and pillows aren't the best in the world but I walked so much in NYC and was so tired at night that I think I could have slept comfortably on a bed of nails, ha ha. The room wasn't huge but it was a decent size. Our room had a queen bed, 2 desks, a small table with 2 chairs, a large TV, a phone, a radio, etc. Also, if you are in your room and need to find where a museum or store is, then use the guide on your tv, it's really convenient. Just turn on the tv and use the remote to go to your city guide and then you can look at museums, restaurants, stores, etc. The area seemed safe and my friend and I didn't have any safety concerns. In fact, during our entire trip almost everyone we encountered was very friendly. There were a couple not-so-friendly people but you find those kinds everywhere (unfortunately). My biggest complaint about NYC in general is that I HATE how everyone expects a tip and how many restaurants calculate a tip in for you. I went to several nice restaurants and they would always bring me my credit card ticket to sign with the price of the meal and the tip included. I have traveled around the world and NYC is one of the only places that does that and I hate it. I know it's tradition but I don't understand why people can't just pay waiters, waitresses, etc. a normal salary and then not have anyone expect a tip. To me a tip is something I give to someone as a gift when the service has been extraordinarily good. But to me, the service at the restaurants that I ate at was nothing special--one of the waiters was downright annoying, but yet he calculated in a $22 tip for himself. I mean, that's crazy. I'm already paying over $150 for a meal and now I have to pay you an additional $22?? why? you didn't do anything for me besides circling my table like a vulture and messing up the order. I don't know. I doubt it's going to change but I like how in Europe nobody expects a tip. You pay the price of the service and that's it. If a meal is $50 then the meal is $50...and not $50 plus a tip of $7.50, etc. That's crazy and I don't understand it. I hear people complain about it all the time but yet it hasn't changed. I dislike it so much. Sorry--back to the hotel---again, it's not the best hotel in the world. If you are looking to be a pampered King or Queen then you should try the Ritz in Central Park or the one in Battery Park or the Four Seasons or Mandarin Oriental, etc. But if you are looking for a decent hotel in a nice area, that's close to everything and for a more affordable price, then the Metro Hotel is a nice choice.

<Author>tazh
<Content>Much more than we expected! We were nervous about choosing a hotel but after reading the reviews here we my husband and I decided on the Hotel Metro. We were so glad we did. We're just average people that stay in average hotels but I was worried about staying in a big city like New York we might end up in a dump. The Hotel Metro was perfect! We were worried about it being a small room but it really wasn't that small. There was room for a queen size bed, TV armoire, 2 nightstands, a small fridge, and even a small table with 2 chairs. The bathroom was plenty big with a shower (not a tub so don't plan on bathing). The bed and pillows weren't the greatest but that wasn't a big deal after we were so tired at the end of each day. Our room was on the 5th floor and I was worried about the noise but there wasn't any. Also I was worried about getting a hotel with good air conditioning since we were there the end of June and the air conditioning was perfect. We could control it and it worked just fine. The workers there were very kind and helpful. The complimentary breakfast was awesome! They had cereal, muffins, pastries, fruit, juice, yogurt, and more and a nice room with several places to sit and TVs with the news on. That definitely saved us money. The hotel is very close to the Empire State Building and there are a couple small stores close to get drinks and snacks to fill up your fridge. There is even a big drug store down the street and around the corner where you can really fill up your fridge. There is a subway stop very very close and we used the subway a lot. Unfortunately there aren't any close restaurants that looked that great. There is a chinese place and some other asian restaurant close and also the Metro Grill is next door but it seemed a little pricey (maybe not for lunch). I would highly recommend staying at the Hotel Metro. You will not be disappointed. If you're concerned about getting a good, clean, decent hotel for your stay in New York the Hotel Metro is for you!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Fantastic place to stay! Two former New Yorkers who returned after 20 years. We spent 5 nights at the end of June at the Metro. This hotel was the perfect place for our return to the city. 1/2 block from subway station that can take you just about anywhere in the city. The room was bigger and more comfortable than we imagined. We stayed on the second floor facing the street and had no noise issues and a great view as well. Macy's, Times Square, World Trade Center, Little Italy and China Town, Central Park, NYC Library and Rockefeller Center all less than 10 min. away. The view of the Empire State Building from the roof top lounge at night was impressive.Our very minor complaints were that there is only one ice/soda machine in the entire hotel and the continental breakfast was o.k. but not a true NY breakfast. <Author>jules_foreva
<Content>Metro Hotel was brilliant! I spent 6 nights at the Metro with my friend (who also wrote a review, dated 19th June) during mid-June 2005 and I must say that this hotel was just great! It's everything that you need in a New York hotel....excellent location (you just can't fault it), great service and polite helpful staff, tasty buffet breakfast and comfortable rooms.It's just a couple of seconds from the subway (a main one - 34th Street - with loads of lines going through it) and is right near Macy's, Empire State Building and not far at all from Times Square (10 mins walk max or one subway stop). We didn't have a view (we stayed on the 3rd floor) but we didn't find it a problem as you're out most of the time and everything else makes up for it! I think that overall this hotel is brilliant and is a perfect place to stay while in New York!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A great find for families My husband and I visited NYC with our two children, 8 and 13, on May 13-16--a time when nearly every other hotel - even the Belvedere, our favorite - was booked up weeks in advance. We were pleasantly surprised with the Metro Hotel. Stayed in a family suite with two spacious sleeping areas...there was plenty of room for all four of us. Bathroom was small (large shower, no tub) but very clean - as was the rest of the room. The free continental breakfast worked out great, and the hotel rooftop was a great spot to have an impromptu picnic lunch with a great view of the Empire State Building. Subway stations were very convenient - as was the original Macys (the wooden escalators were a big hit). The $250 a night pricetag was more than we would normally pay, but for our kids' first trip to NYC it was worth it.

<Content>Perfect for our family of 4!! We checked out of the Hotel Metro this morning (June 1, 2005) thoroughly satisfied with our 2-night stay. I would stay there again. We had no street noise, no rude service, no problems whatsoever. And like I said, our room was huge.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Fantastic Hotel - Perfect Location!!! I just got back from NYC today and stayed at the Metro Hotel for 5 nights from Tuesday 24th to Sunday 29th May. I am proud to say that this hotel is absolutely fantastic! I booked a standard room and having read previous reviews that the rooms can be quite small, looking on the flooring plan for the 5th floor, our room was indicated the smallest but it was certainly big enough for me and my partner along with a queen size bed, table  2 chairs, chest of drawers, TV with 30 channels, fridge and wall closet to hide your suitcases and shopping bags. I would say compared to british standards, this would be a medium sized room to me, probably known as a New York small to them. Our bathroom was quite small but due to the lack of space it was cute and cosy and certainly makes up for it's brilliant spacious shower with glass doors (can fit 2!), basin, toilet, huge mirror, good lighting, hair dryer, air ventilator, fresh towels and nicely decorated in marble decor. I also love the free complimentary breakfast in the morning with a good choice of muffins, bagels, danish pastries, cereals, fruit, yogurts and unlimited juice, tea and coffee. Plus free tea and coffee is also available throughout the day in the executive louge which was an extra bonus. The hotel is perfectly located in an excellent location, a quick 5 second walk to the 35th subway, minutes from Macy's and within walking distance to all the shops and surrounding cafe's in Herald Square and 10minutes walk to Times Square.For a budget hotel, I love the art decor, the simplicity, price and location of this hotel, the staff are very friendly and I'll definently be staying at this hotel again.

<Content>Absolutely loved the Metro!! We stayed at the Metro Hotel May 5 -10 2005. It was our first trip to NYC and booked the Metro based on price and location. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Sorely Disappointed This was our third trip to NYC in the past year. Previously we enjoyed terrific stays at the Doubletree Suites Times Square and the lovely Omni Berkshire Hotel. On this trip, since we would be staying 10 days, we were trying to find a reasonably priced and well located hotel. After much research, we settled on the Hotel Metro which seemed it would match our needs. Several times prior to arrival, I called and requested a quiet room based on reports I'd read on Tripadvisor. Upon arrival, after a sleepless night on the plane from California, we were told we would have to wait a number of hours for our room. Spent time enjoying Macy's which is very nearby. After dozing off in the hotel lobby, we were finally taken to our room one floor beneath the Penthouse. I knew that the hotel was undergoing construction and questioned whether or not this would be a quiet room. We were reassured by the front desk that there wouldn't be any hammering or drilling. Quite the contrary! We had barely closed our eyes for a badly needed nap when a power drill began in the room to one side and a jackhammer in the room on the other. Above us, a marble floor was being pounded into place. Leaving our room, I stepped over power cords and equipment en route to the elevator. After speaking with the front desk we were given a key to another room. Upon moving our suitcases to this room (which was a fraction of the size...not that the first room was spacious!) we discovered that our new room had not even been cleaned yet. We were shown one other room where the double bed was literally less than one foot from the door to the hallway. (More like what one would find in a motel, I think.) The front desk was not particularly helpful explaining that the hotel was full. Clearly if your hotel is full, you don't worry about unhappy guests. The frosting on the cake for me at the Metro, was when we tried at 10:30 pm the next night to find the ice machine which was unavailable due to the construction. We were told by the front desk that we could bring our ice bucket downstairs and ask at the restaurant next door for some ice! (My daughter immediately marched downstairs in her pj's, ice bucket in hand, and gave the front desk crew quite a shock!) Since we were to be staying for 10 days and our trip was getting off to a bad start, I had my husband in California go on Priceline and bid on a room for us at a different hotel. We spent only 2 nights at the Metro before moving to the wonderful Intercontinental Barclay for the remaining 8 nights. I cannot begin to emphasize the difference. The service, class and ammenties were apparent as soon as we entered the lobby. We slept in total comfort and quiet in a king size bed in a wonderfully large room at a 4 Diamond Hotel well located near Rockefeller Center FOR THE SAME PRICE as what we were paying at the Metro!!! Upon checking out of the Metro, I expressed our disappointment to the Manager who offered absolutely NO compensation or apologies. When I mentioned the incident with the ice, he said Well, what would you have us do? I promptly told him that what I would have him do is suggest that his staff offer to bring some ice up to their guests in this situation, not the other way around. This is NOT what I call customer service and I have worked in a customer service business for more than 30 years. In fairness to the Metro, the breakfast is fairly good and there is a bit of charm to the Art Deco decor. The rooms are very small however and the bathrooms are tiny. Our bed was NOT comfortable and it was difficult to get the room a comfortable temperature. The noise level was definitely UNBEARABLE for us. Above all, the management needs to make SERIOUS effort at realizing that without satisfied customers, the Metro has nothing. Obviously, many people find low cost  location overriding factors. I, for one, also appreciate customer service and comfort and with so many hotels to choose from in a city of this size would never recommend this hotel to anyone except someone who is searching for a low price at the expense of sacrificing other ammenities.I totally love NYC and have found people on the street to be very kind  helpful. On my list of must sees in NYC: the Metropolitan Museum of Art, the Museum of Modern Art, Central Park, Ellis Island  Statue of Liberty, Grand Central, Times Square  as many Broadway shows as your budget will allow. The wait to go up in the Empire State Bldg can be harrowing, but the view is worth seeing once. On our last trip, we had drinks in the Rainbow Room with a fabulous sunset view looking across at the Empire State Building and I enjoyed that much more. Also, the Observatory Tour of the State of Liberty is very interesting. For anyone with immigrant parents or relatives, Ellis Island is quite amazing. I was thrilled to be able to list my mother's name on the Immigrant Wall of Honor there. Definitely a special moment for me. NYC has far too many good restaurants to name, but the prix fix menus at many are a real bargain. Some of our recommendations include: DB Bistro, Lombardi's Pizza, Serendipity (order the frozen Hot Chocolate!), 21 Club, Bubby's, Acqua Pazza, and definitely brunch at Sarabeth's. NYC definitely is one AMAZING city and we are huge fans!

It is within walking distance to the Empire State Building, Times Square, Madison Square Garden, Macy's and most important of all, the subway station at Herald Square. <Content>Good hotel in a great location Just returned from a 5 day trip (12 - 17th April '05), here are my thoughts...Location: Excellent - Macys and Empire State  5 mins, Times Square 5 to 10mins.Cleanliness: Excellent, room was cleaned each day and had fresh towels. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Location, Great Hotel My friend and I stayed here from March 30th until April 5th, and we were not at all disapointed. Check in was easy, and the staff were very helpful with any questions that I had. We had room 201, which was just at the top of the small staircase, which goes round the reception.The room was very spacious, and was better than what we expected! The bathroom was very clean, and had all the usual amenities (soap, shampoo etc). Even though we didn't use it, it was nice to have a working fridage there too, which, I must say, didn't make any noise!I was woken up once or twice by the traffic just outside, as our room was facing the front. It didn't bother us too much though, I guess that's just typical New York traffic!The complimentery breakfast was nice and light, was simply a choice of muffins, bagels etc, and cereal. I found this to be enough, as there are many places in NY to eat durnig the day, and the portions are huge anyway, so we didn't need too much for breakfast. It was nice also having the TV's on the walls too, to catch up on the news or whatever.When the room was cleaned, it was cleaned up to a very high standard. The location of the hotel is perfect. It is literally a 1 minute walk from the Empire State Building, and a 10 minute walk from Times Square. Macy's Department Store was also just at the end of the road, along with many other shops (in particular GAP and Foot Locker).I am very glad I stayed at the Metro Hotel, and would definitely consider staying here again.

<Author>Matt1976
<Content>A great little hotel! Stayed at the Metro Hotel for 7 nights between 30th March - 6th April 2005. Upon arrival check-in was very swift. I had emailed the hotel earlier to request a larger room as I'm very tall. They were very happy to accomodate this request. We were given a room on the 11th floor which was spacious and clean. The bathrooms are lovely, all in marble with a great walk in shower. Each morning while taking a shower I'd look out of the window and see the Empire State Building! What a great way to wake up each morning! The fridge was handy to have as we could store water and other drinks. Also in the room was a small lounge area with 2 chairs, a writing table, drawers, large TV and enough closet space with an iron/ironing board stored here. The free breakfast in the morning was great. Went here a few times while staying here. Nothing fancy just bagels, muffins, fruit, coffee/tea. Handy if you just wanted something light to eat. Did a lot of eating in New York so a light breakfast sometimes was just what the doctor ordered! The staff were all very helpful and kind. I would stay here again as the hotel is exceptionally clean and centrally located. I always felt safe when returning in the evening which was nice. I would have given this hotel 5 stars but the beds were a little soft. Nothing too annoying - we soon got used to them! If you are thinking of staying at the Metro you won't be disappointed. A real bargain here and I look forward to staying there again very soon.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Ideal Location!! Above average Hotel for the location! Stayed last week (Spring Break...yikes). The hotel is located perfectly...on 35th just a few minutes walk from Penn Station, Times Square/Theatre District, Macy's, Subway lines, 5th Ave, etc.The room was sparse or shall we say minimalist, but clean and well kept. Beds were very average but sufficiently comfortable. We were initially given a very small, dark room on the 3rd floor with views of nothing. We asked for a different room and ended up higher on the 11th floor which afforded a slightly larger/brighter room with views of other buildings. In my view (especially in N.Y.) location is everything! And this hotel has the location without a doubt. The morning/afternoon staff is measurably friendlier and more readily attentive/informative then their PM counterparts...so get your info from the morning crew! A few hints: The Red Bar right next door has a great atmosphere and staff for pre/post evening cocktails. Guisseppes Pizza on the corner has great pizza by the slice in a hunger pinch. PAX Deli (all over Midtown area) great, inexpensive food. The Blue Fin on Times Square is fun, upscale and semi-affordable for dinner and cocktails with the big city vibe. Could go on and on, but you'll figure it out from here...Enjoy!!

<Author>Coxy
<Content>disappointed Booked the Metro because of all the good reviews we have read over the last few years. Stayed 14th March for 4 nights. Room was large enough for the 2 of us and clean, fridge was supplied but no in room safe. Staff were helpful and polite and breakfast was excellent, along with the muffins, pastries and bagels they also supply toast, cereal and yoghurt. Free coffee and juice all day is also a bonus. After reading previous posts which stated the lower 8 floors had been renovated recently we requested a low floor and were given room number 204, (did not look as though it had been recently refurbished). Another post mentioned the excessive noise level on the lower floors but as I could only find the 1 post about this I assumed the person was just being 'picky'. Well, he was absolutely right - dustcarts at 1.30  4.30, delivery lorries etc. It was unbearable. Don't get me wrong, I know NYC is a noisy city, this was my 3rd visit but I have never encountered anything like it. We tried to move to a higher floor but there was nothing available. This did affect our stay and our view of the hotel. Judging by all the other reviews we were just unlucky, as a whole the hotel has everything you need for a short stay but we would think twice about staying there again.

<Author>spa11
<Content>Great family hotel We just returned from a quick, 4-day trip to NYC and had a great experience at the Hotel Metro. Being Spring Break and St. Patrick's Day Parade week, we had a tough time finding a midtown hotel that would take the five of us - 2 adults and 3 children. I spent 8 hours online shopping hotels and comparing prices and reviews. The Hotel Metro's family suite is ideal. We were in room #806. It includes an enormous bedroom with two doubles for the kids and a second private bedroom with a queen for us. Kitchenette, 2 tv's, large bathroom, nice desk with lots of lamps, great windows that open fully and overlook the Empire State Building. Every inch was sparkling clean (and we are picky). The housekeepers are exceptional. Not a hair or a scuff mark or the hint that anyone else ever stayed in the room. The hotel offers a nice, quick continental breakfast with long hours and in a roomy lounge area. Complimentary NY Times. Around the clock coffee and tea. Great location just a few steps from Macy's and 7 blocks to Times Square. The staff was helpful and always available. When we had to get to the airport in the middle of the St. Patrick's day parade, the doorman actually found us a cab and had it waiting for us when we returned from a last-second shopping trip. When you read reviews that describe a hotel as good or roomy by New York City standards, understand that this place is good and roomy by any standards. Make your reservation and quit worrying.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>It is what it is.... That is -- the Hotel Metro is a moderately priced hotel in midtown Manhattan. If you set your expectaions somewhere around the Holiday Inn level, you'll be perfectly satisfied with this hotel. However, if you're expecting to find four or five-star luxury at this price range (at this or any other hotel), prepare to be sorely disappointed.  There is no question that this hotel has some nice features and added touches. The lobby is certainly above average at this price point, as reported by previous guests. The bagels, muffins and pastries served each morning are fresh and plentiful, and the quality of the coffee is pleasantly surprising. The fitness facility is also better than expected -- most gym regulars should be able to get a decent workout here with only a few compromises to their regular regimen. Finally, the view from the rooftop patio may alone be worth the price of admission -- it is indeed breathtaking.  The rooms are miniscule, without question. I've stayed in quite a few NYC hotels and I've grown accustomed to the small room sizes, but this was SMALL. I get the impression (based upon other reviews) that room sizes vary significantly within the standard size, so this may be something to discuss with the front desk at check-in. In my case, there was barely enough room between the bed and the door for the door to swing open, and the chair and tables which nestled against the window on the opposite side of the room came right to the other edge of the bed. Door, bed, table, window -- that's it. The aforementioned window, furthermore, took a fair bit of effort to open, and there was no screen. I'd be surprised if the entire room was more than 50 or 60 square feet in size. All this notwithstanding, the room was reasonably well decorated, and didn't feel at all shabby or poorly maintained. The bathroom, though tiny as well, was nicely appointed with marble throughout, and the standup shower had excellent water pressure.  A final word with regards to the bed. This was my greatest source of disappointment with the Hotel Metro. The bed (advertised as a Queen) was barely a double, and it was likely the least comfortable I've ever slept in. The springs jutted up throughout the mattress, and I woke up with an aching back each morning. The pillows were tiny as well -- they were more along the lines of those mini airline pillows than those normally found on a bed.  All in all, I would recommend this hotel to budget-minded travellers. In its price range, I'm not certain one could do too much better in midtown Manhattan. Those in search of a bit more luxury, however, should look elsewhere.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Be careful what room, and what day The staff are nice, and it is convenient. The free breakfast is nice as well as a free New York Times. I would recommend, however, you ask to see the room you get before signing in.  I stayed on a Wednesday night and my room was on the fourth floor. It was garbage collection night and right across the street from the Metro Hotel is a huge, and I mean huge stop. For one hour between 10:30 PM and 11:30 PM they noisily loaded clanking dumpsters and mountains of trash bags into trash trucks. Then the next morning from 6-7 AM the dumpsters were noisly redistributed to their owners. If the hotel windows were better sealed some of this noise might have been lessened. But still, that was an awful experience.  The bed in which I slept actually had springs that could be felt. The refrigerator is just two feet from the bed and makes a lot of noise, especially when turning on. I turned it off for the night. The bed sheets were not even tucked in, so when I get off the bed I had to smooth them out before getting back in.   I also requested a non-smoking room, but got a smoking room.   Considering convenience and price, if the hotel stay had been nicer I would have stayed there many nights over the next few months, but I have switched to another hotel.

<Author>pumfster
<Content>Lovely little hotel in the centre of it all!! Just returned from a 4 night stay at the metro. This is a great value hotel right in the centre of New York only a 2 minute walk from Macy's and The Empire State building. It's not a luxury hotel by far but it is very friendly and cosy. There are currently some building works going on at the hotel but this did not cause any inconvience and soon there will be a lovely new breakfast room there. The free breakfasts are great and we ate there every morning, there is orange juice, tea/coffee and also bagels, muffins and danish pastries!! yum yum!! The rooms are quite small here, well ours was anyway but it was clean and warm (which was great as is was well below freezing outside!!). You also get all the free shampoo's, shower gel etc so do not bother taking any!All in all we had a great time at the Metro and I would recommend it to anybody looking for a good value hotel in the centre of new york!!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>I Love the Metro I have stayed at the Metro 4 times, most recently 16th - 21st Dec 2004. Its location is excellent, just off 5th Avenue and within easy walking distance of Macy's, Empire State Building and Times Square, and a pleasant stroll up 5th Ave to Central Park.The hotel lobby is beautiful, the staff is very pleasant and knowledgeable and the rooms are spotlessly clean. I am the fussiest person in the world for cleanliness and there wasn't a speck of dirt anywhere.I went with 3 friends and we had 2 twin rooms. Our room was not the biggest I've ever stayed in but it certainly wasn't the smallest, and our friends' room was a very good size. We had no problems getting our requested twin rooms, despite booking over the internet (not with the hotel).Comparing the hotel with when I have stayed before (1996, 1998  1999) I will say that our room and corridors looked a little tired, although certainly not tatty. I believe there has been refurbishment up to the 8th floor and we were on the 9th. And you do have to wait 2 or 3 minutes for a lift at busy times.I would always go back to the Metro as I think you can pay a lot more for the same in New York.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>There are better mid-priced options My husband and I spent two nights at the Metro Hotel just before Christmas; we booked the hotel based on reviews posted here. We would definitely not recommend the hotel--there are much better hotels in New York in a similar price range.Although the lobby is quite nice, the hotel's efforts ended there. The elevator carpet was worn and dirty,the staff wasn't very friendly (they were never rude, but barely cracked a smile), and, more importantly, the bed was the most uncomfortable that we'd slept on--the mattress was old and lumpy, so every time we turned over we felt every spring. We woke up tired both days, which was detrimental to our enjoyment of the city. Also, the shower walls in our bathroom were moldy and the shower floor cracked and badly stained. And this was after changing from the first room that we were given (1101), which looked like a prison cell. The free breakfast was really not an advantage--nothing you couldn't get on the street for $2 or less (muffins, bagels, juice and coffee--and they didn't even have a toaster for the bagels). If we hadn't prepaid for two nights we would have definitely changed hotels after the first night. I've stayed at the Park South Hotel and the Roger Williams, both moderately priced and inclusive of breakfast, and enjoyed much better accomodations and service.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Fabulous hotel; would stay there again! My husband and I decided to stay at the Hotel Metro during our recent December trip to NYC. We were more than happy with the hotel, and would highly recommend this hotel to others. In October we stated at a W hotel in NYC and preferred the Metro, which was also less expensive for a better room.Check-in at the hotel was seamless, and though we booked online through the hotel's website there was no problem with our reservation. In fact, they even upgraded us for free to a better room, for no apparent reason. The room we ended up with was fabulous--huge (the size of my entire apartment), with a nice bathroom and plenty of closet space. For what we were paying we were very pleased. Everything was clean and spotless and the maid service was excellent.We also liked the intimate feel of the Metro, over more impersonal hotels like the major chains. We didn't have much interaction with the staff, though they did stow our luggage on the last day because we had a late flight and there was no problem with this. We enjoyed the free continental breakfast, and ate onc breakfast in the adjoining hotel restaurant, which was good and inexpensive, though the service was painfully slow.The location was excellent too, and we thought we got a lot of bang for our buck staying there. While the elevators were tiny and infrequent, we had the same problem with the W. Overall, we were extremely pleased with our Hotel Metro experience, and would recommend it above the W anytime (the only other NYC hotel we have experience with.) Staying there made our vacation hassle-free and extremely enjoyable.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Good Hotel, Great Location My friend  I spent Nov 18-21 in Manhattan, staying at the Hotel Metro (located on 34th street b/w 5th  6th.) After doing MUCH research on where to stay that was reasonably priced (read lots of reviews), I choose this hotel and can honestly say that I was very pleasantly surprised. The hotel itself was clean, decorated well, centrally located and the staff was VERY friendly. We didn't spend that much time in the room as there is so much to do in NY but it was clean and comfortable and it had a refrigerator, which was a plus. The only negatives I have is that the bathroom shower was VERY narrow  hard to move in (we're petite girls)so if you are of a heavier set, it could cause quite a problem. The complimentary breakfast was OK -  the restaurant on site wasn't bad. The hotel itself is less than a block away from Macy's  other shops like Gap, Vicky's, Express, HM, Steve Madden, Deane Pharmacy and more. It is 1 block away from the Empire State Bldg  about 6-8 blocks from Times Square. A couple of bars are located on the same street of the hotel as well as Subway, a Chinese place and nearby is McDonald's, Burger King  Wendy's. Around the corner on 35th street is Keene Steakhouse - which has excellent fillet, if you are looking for a very nice place to have dinner. Definitely recommend the hotel if you are looking for a reasonably priced place where you can lay your head down after a long day of being out and about on the town.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Excellent Location I've just returned from my first and long awaited visit to the Big Apple staying at the Metro Hotel from 24th-28th Sept 04 - the whole trip from beginning to end was absolutely fantastic! The hotel was in a superb location -Times Sq  Broadway a 10min walk away; Macy's  Empire State Building even closer at 5 mins! The staff were great (a particular thank you to George and Mike if you're reading this!) We asked if we could change our room after realising we hadn't got a street view and were moved to the 7th floor at the front of the hotel with no problems at all (you therefore might wanna bear this in mind when booking - ask for a room at the front of the hotel overlooking the street, although both rooms were twin, the one at the front was much much bigger). I agree that furnishings could be updated in rooms but that really is my only criticism. On the day of departure we booked a taxi through the hotel to take us to the airport at a flat rate of $80 - a huge black stretch limo turned up although we hadn't booked it! Not sure if this was a fluke but we definitely didnt request it. Was worth it though so again you may wanna bear that in mind. During our 5 day stay we managed to do Empire State Building, shopping on 5th Avenue, a helicoptor and harbour tour, open top bus tours, Statue of Liberty, Ground Zero, Times Square, show on Broadway........my legs are starting to ache again just writing about it! Every ache and pain I felt after such a hectic weekend though was worth it. I would highly recommend arriving with a list of stuff you wanna do/see and speak to your hotel on arrival about the best way to do it. The staff at Metro at least were very helpful and made sure we got to do and see everything in a way best suited to us ($tips always help of course!) I think I've waffled on enough now so on a final note - enjoy it!Danielle xx

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Good Value, great location Located between 5th and 6th Ave, this hotel has a great location. Easy walk to Times Square to the north and Greenwich Village to the south. Room was small but clean. Staff very attentive and helpful. Nice open-air rooftop bar to have late night drink and a nice view of the Empire State Building. Staff very helpful in supplying maps and giving directions. This hotel attracts a lot of European tourists who I suspect get the scoop from the internet. We would definitely stay there again because of the location. My wife is usually fussier than me about hotels and she would like to return there. We booked on Orbitz for around $200/might for a Friday, Saturday and Sunday stay. Also, right around the corner is a 24 hour convenience store which is really convenient. Stocks not only food but band-aids etc and all the little things you might need last minute.

The reception look very nice and the staff equally helpful and nice, although I was told the hotel manager was the person on reception. We were given our keys and made our way up to our room. We were on the 12th floor and I thought brilliant we will have some peace and should have a good view. What a mistake of thinking that!!! When we got in to our pokey room that you couldn't swing a cat in, I thought we were out on the street, lorries below were loading up and banging their doors closed, their brakes sweaking loudly every 5 mins. I thought the window was open and asked my husband to close it. It was open at the top, my husband tried to close it but it was stuck. He asked me to help, we both tried pushing the window up but the window fell out of the frame and crashed down onto the air conditioning unit!!! The frame was so heavy he couldn't put it back in, luckily the window fell in towards us and not out onto the street!!! I rang down to reception and told them their window had fallen out the frame, they didnt believe me. Someone came up and accused my husband of pulling it out of the frame! He was so rude and arrogant, we explained that the window wasnt closed and we wanted to close it because of the noise, he again accused us doing it ourselves, tell me why would I want to pull a window out of its frame, espeicially as both of us together couldn't lift it let alone pulling it out!! I went down to reception and asked to swap rooms. A good tip for all - Ask for the keys first to view the room, check that everything is ok then confirm that you'll have it!! Thats what we did after the incident with the window. We changed rooms, again the room was pokey and if you crunched your neck, you could just see the Empire State building. The bathroom door would not close as the door was too big to get pass the toilet. But all in all the hotel was ok. It was clean, free coffee in the mornings with bagels. If you're on a budget then this is the place to stay. A good location. I personally would not stay here again.  
<Date>Sep 5, 2004

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great location and price with an authentic NYC vibe I stayed at the Hotel Metro last weekend, June 17-20,2004. I too was a bit leery reading the reviews on this site, but found the hotel to offer a true New York experience that I doubt could be found at most large, popular chains. For the $150/night we paid for the room on hotels.com, we were thoroughly satisfied and would stay there again.The hotel is a meer 4-5 blocks from Penn Station and Times Square, and less than one block from 5th avenue, on the edge of the Fashion District. The decor is a sophisticated and sexy art deco style, themed around film stars of the 1930's. The waitstaff was prompt and pleasant during all exchanges.The rooms were well appointed but small. Accomodations were clean and comfortable, and the bathrooms boasted a refreshingly different rose marble decor with a fully enclosed glass shower. There is a rather large refrigerator in the room as well, an expected bonus in a downtown NYC hotel!Besides an interesting decor in the lobby and rooms, the hotel offered several other interesting areas for gathering and entertainment. There is an attached restaurant/bar next door called the Metro Grill. The atmosphere was pleasant, the barstaff friendly and quite generous :) There is also a rooftop bar, with an extremely upclose view of the uppermost towers of the Empire State building (which is on the next block). To our disappointment, the rooftop bar was not in operation during our entire stay, which was over a weekend. The nights were rather cool however, which may explain why. The hotel also had a well appointed rooftop gym.Overall, our stay at the Hotel Metro was excellent and I highly recommend it. However, due to the size of the rooms and overall theme, I do not recommend this as a family hotel. For couples looking for a sophisticated, sexy theme in the heart of Manhattan, it's a sure bet. Also, priced $50-150/night cheaper than many other downtown NYC hotels, it is an excellent bargain.  
<Date>Jun 27, 2004

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Won't stay here again I attended a day and a half conference in New York City recently and stayed two nights at the Hotel Metro. Given the great reviews and the suggestion from the conference organizers, I thought it was a good choice. The location was great and well within walking distance of the conference and the Empire State Building. However, the room was tiny and of Days Inn quality. The carpet was dirty and the building smelled of cigarette smoke ( I know people on the east coast smoke in the buildings unlike the L.A. area), but it was bothersome. I also didn't see any rampsfor people who use wheelchairs or scooters and the building and elevators would not accomodate a person with a disability easily. Staff was friendly enough and had good ideas about what shows to see and things to do while in the city. This hotel would not be my choice for my next trip to NYC and oh, I haven't slept on box springs in twenty five years!

<Content>It was far better than we were expecting We booked a trip to NY for my wife, myself and brother and sister-in-laws. It was a deal with BA. One piece of advice... If your going to NY stay at the Metro, good Value for money.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Value  Stayed at the Metro in Sept 03 on our first trip to NY. Excellent midtown location just one block from Macys, with very helpful and pleasant staff. Great value for the 5 nights we stayed. Roof top terrace on 12th floor is a must, as it's in the next street to the Empire State so you look straight up at it from the terrace. Room was good sized double with well appointed bathroom and more TV channels than you've ever seen. Breakfast room is excellent with enough bagels, muffins, jucies etc to fill you for the day and a constant, free supply of coffee available all day. Will certainly use the Metro in future. (Don't miss the revolving cocktail bar on 49th floor of Time Square Marriot Hotel too!)
